Wuhan Cracks Down on Multiple Kidnapping Cases

Eight Bandits/Communists Executed

Hankou Correspondence: Wuhan is an important town on the Yangtze River, with a mix of Chinese and foreigners. Many bandits use concessions as safe havens to secretly plot activities. The Wuhan Garrison Headquarters, through strict vigilance, has successively cracked down on no less than dozens of bandit/communist organizations. Recently, two more kidnapping cases were cracked, and eight bandits/communists were executed, further stabilizing the market order. Earlier, in the Wudaocun area of the 37th district of Wuchang County, several bandits kidnapped Wu Chuanxue and his wife from Wu Hongfa's store. Wu's wife was rescued by the defense team, but Wu was taken to Han (Hankou) and a ransom of twelve thousand dollars was demanded, to be exchanged at the Pinghan Railway's Chenjiaji north of Dazhimen. However, Wu was taken to Han and, while the bandits went ashore to buy food, he seized the opportunity to escape and reported to the third district that the bandit den was near Baofu Temple. The district sent Wu to the Wuchang County Office, and with the help of the regular team, three communist bandits who colluded with kidnappers, Zuo Yurong, Chen Guohua, and Xu Qingfu, were arrested at Baofu Temple. According to their confessions, the bandit leader moved to a concession in Hankou and admitted to joining the Communist Party. They were then sent to the garrison headquarters by the county office for interrogation. At the same time, the kidnapping of a child surnamed Wang occurred in Lijiaqiao, Qianjiajie, and Taiping Township in Wuchang County. The countryside clearing bureau sent a team to apprehend the criminals, first capturing Hu Doufu and Yang Zhifa, followed by Zhu Lianrui in Zhifang, Yang Yurong outside the Dazhimen Railway in Hankou, Fang De'en, Zhou Xingfu, Wang Baoshan, and Li Xiushan in Yangjiawei, Mei Er, Mei Ruiyuan, and Mei Ruixuan in Jinkou, Zhang Yuan in the dike factory, and Li Shunquan and Huang Wanxing in a smoking den. In total, seventeen kidnappers were apprehended in Wuhan, all of whom were sent to the garrison headquarters for interrogation. Those who confessed without hesitation, such as Zuo Yurong, have been executed. Their crimes are as follows: (1) The Hankou Public Security Bureau presented three kidnappers, Liu Mingshan, Chen Yaoqing, and Yuan Zenan, and the Wuchang County Government presented two communist bandits who colluded with kidnappers, Zuo Yurong and Chen Guohua. The criminal Liu Mingshan had colluded with Qian Xingwu and others to kidnap Huang Dongshan, a wealthy household in Suizhou, and killed Dongshan. He then sneaked into Hankou to participate in robbing money houses. Zuo Yurong and Chen Guohua were both communist bandits who colluded with Chen Yaoqing and Yuan Zenan to rob the Wu family. Their crimes were serious and all were sentenced to death. (2) The Headquarters Inspection Office arrested a bandit, Liu Guanghua. According to his confession, he joined the "White Wolf" bandits in the early years of the Republic and disturbed the five provinces of Shanxi, Shaanxi, Henan, Anhui, and Hubei. After the "White Wolf" bandits were eliminated, he was wanted in his native Yingshan. He hid in the army and later lived in Liujiamiao in Hankou, colluding with bandits and dividing the spoils. He should be sentenced to death according to the law. (3) The Headquarters Inspection Office presented Chen Youzhang, a communist bandit from Tongshan who was hiding in Hanyang. According to his confession, he served as the chairman of the puppet soviet government and the chairman of the riot committee in Gaokengbu, the fifth district of Tongshan. He led the crowd to break into the city, burned down government offices, and released prisoners many times. He kidnapped people for ransom and confiscated countless properties, killing hundreds of people. His actions were shocking and he should be sentenced to death according to the law. (4) According to the Wuchang Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, the bandit Yang Guixiang was arrested. According to her confession, she communicated with bandits and initially robbed merchant Chen Sanyuan and others of cash and promissory notes on the road in Jiayu. Later, she openly went to Yingwuzhou to redeem the promissory notes. She should be sentenced to death according to the law for punishing bandits. (May 19th)

Tang Kesan Discusses Methods for Mediating the Kang-Tibet Dispute

Chengdu Correspondence: Tang Kesan, Director of General Affairs of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, and Liu Zanting, a specialist of the Commission and former commander of the Sichuan-Tibet Han Army, and Tang Musheng, a Kang-Tibet inspection commissioner, who were sent by the central government to Xikang to mediate the property dispute between Dajin Temple and Bai Lishi's office, arrived in Rong (Chengdu) on the 3rd of the month and stayed at the Military Academy Research Association of the 24th Army. Tang made a statement regarding the Da-Bai case, the main points of which are as follows: (1) In the Da-Bai property dispute, the Dalai Lama believes that such matters are extremely common in Kang-Tibet and can easily be resolved within the sect without involving the government. The local government of Xikang believes that when people file such lawsuits, it cannot ignore them and shirk its responsibility. Those who are unreasonable and rely on strength to disobey should naturally be sanctioned. The central government believes that the Dalai Lama is currently demonstrating sincerity, and the settlement methods for the Panchen Lama and Nuona Lama have not yet been agreed upon. If the central government does not make concessions and show leniency, the Dalai Lama will suspect that the central government is outwardly agreeing to allegiance but secretly ordering troops to advance. A small impatience will lead to major chaos. Therefore, the central government has repeatedly issued strict orders to restrain the officers and soldiers from starting another war. If the Tibetan troops disobey the restraint and continue to advance, the fault lies with the Dalai Lama, and it will not be too late to issue an explicit order for suppression. (2) Since the property dispute occurred, the Dalai Lama was confused by the one-sided statements of Dajin Temple and the troops stationed in Kang-Tibet, and failed to prevent the troops stationed in Kang-Tibet from assisting the rebel actions. After receiving the central government's order to stop military actions on both sides and wait for officials to be sent for fair resolution, the Dalai Lama ordered the Changdu Kalon to order Degge Gutong Daiben to withdraw his troops, and telegraphed the central government to welcome the dispatch of officials to Kang to resolve the issue in accordance with the order. Therefore, I was ordered to travel to Sichuan as soon as possible. Once my luggage arrives from Chongqing in a few days, I will rush to the front line to relieve the people of Kang from their suffering as soon as possible. (3) Before both parties hold their own views and the actual situation is not fully understood, I will never prejudge the solution with preconceived notions. Even if a solution is proposed in the future, it must be submitted to the central government for explicit instructions. I cannot act arbitrarily. Whether the Dalai Lama's sincerity towards the central government is genuine or not will be observed in this matter. As for the mediation method, the first step is to directly negotiate with the Kalon, ordering them to defend their original defense and restore the situation before the war. The second step is to investigate where Da-Bai's right and wrong lies, and fairly mediate so that both sides are satisfied. Otherwise, I will only report the actual situation to the central government and listen to the truth. In short, I have no definite certainty at the moment as to what extent I will be able to do in the future, but I must go deep into Zi or Degge and do my best to live up to the people of Kang and the party and country.

Shocking News of Haiyuan Pavilion's Book Collection Falling into Foreign Hands

Brokered by Pan Fu to be Sold to the Japanese

Most of it has been shipped from Tianjin to Dalian

Shandong Education Department Published a Statement Warning

Jinan Correspondence: The Liancheng Yang family's Haiyuan Pavilion book collection, except for those that have been damaged or sold, is now stored in Jinan and Tianjin. The ones in Tianjin are mostly famous Song and Yuan editions, of immense value. The ones in Jinan are ordinary books, unimportant. The Ministry of Education and the Shandong Education Department were deeply concerned that the books would fall into foreign hands. The Shandong Provincial Library Director Wang Xiantang was instructed to draft the "Draft Outline of the Agreement on Yang's Haiyuan Pavilion Books" to preserve the books. The methods include Yang entrusting the library to preserve them on his behalf, or semi-donating and semi-selling, or the government purchasing them at a fair price, asking the book owner Yang Jingfu to choose one. Yang expressed his willingness to accept the second semi-donation and semi-sale method. Although the two sides have not yet had formal negotiations, indirect contacts have been made several times. Wang Xiantang also planned to go to Tianjin in the near future to formally consult with Yang and investigate the number of books and agree on the price so that this issue can be resolved as soon as possible. Unexpectedly, it was recently learned that the books were sold to the Japanese through Pan Fu's introduction. The matter concerns the loss of Chinese cultural relics, which is quite shocking. According to a letter received by the Shandong Provincial Library Director Wang Xiantang from Tianjin, Yang's Haiyuan Pavilion collection has recently been mortgaged to a certain bank for 400,000 yuan through Pan Fu's introduction. In other words, it was sold to a certain bank. It is reported that the books have recently been transferred from Tianjin to Dalian via the post office. The buyer is Japanese, and the transaction will be formally concluded soon. After receiving the letter, Wang reported it to the Education Department. The Education Department decided to publish a warning in the Tianjin and Jinan newspapers, stating that the Haiyuan Pavilion collection is related to Chinese culture and is the property of China. Shandong should have the priority to purchase when Yang sells it. During this negotiation period, foreigners must not buy or sell it without authorization. At the same time, Library Director Wang Xiantang was sent to Tianjin to investigate the truth. Wang was ordered to set off north on the 20th. It is reported that the reason why Yang sold the books to the Japanese this time was that he feared that selling to domestic government agencies would result in a loss in price. Selling to the Japanese would get a higher price. Therefore, after the government agencies proposed a method a few days ago, foreign and Chinese book dealers continued to visit Yang's door to negotiate purchases. (May 18th)

The Dangerous State of Northeast Rural Areas

Groups of Poor People Break into Rich Families for Food

Shenyang Correspondence: Northeast rural areas have recently entered a dangerous state. According to investigations by those who have experienced the situation firsthand, it has reached a point where it is full of tragic scenes and the sound of wailing. Generally speaking, the rural areas in various parts of Northeast China are extremely exhausted. However, if we analyze it, their current situation has different points. On the one hand, they suffer from having abundant grain in storage but difficult to find customers. On the other hand, they are plagued by lack of food to feed their families or lack of seeds to cultivate the fields. This contradictory phenomenon is most prominent in the disaster areas of western Liaoning. For more than a month, the so-called "eating big families" (吃大家, meaning poor people gathering to eat at rich people's houses) trend has occurred successively in various places. Because it is currently the spring plowing season, most poor households not only lack seeds for plowing but also lack food to feed their families. Therefore, they support the old and carry the young, forming groups and going to rich people's houses to eat together. The number of people is as many as several thousand, and as few as several hundred. Those responsible for maintaining law and order are also unable to take action, resulting in the poor becoming even poorer, and the rich also becoming poor. Counties such as Liaoyuan, Tongliao, Shuangshan, Kangping, and Faku in Liaoning Province, and Fuxin and Chaoyang in Rehe Province, are particularly tragic. It is reported that due to the continuous rain and disaster last year in Shuangshan County, the autumn harvest was less than one-tenth of previous years. Officials and people are in extreme distress. Police and education salaries have been in arrears for several months, and it is almost impossible to cook. Currently, about half of the rural households in the four townships lack seeds and food. Between April 22nd and 26th, five days, several groups of poor people crowded into the county seat to demand food. Each group numbered from more than 1,000 to 2,000 or 3,000. In Tongliao County, two groups of poor people "eating big families" also appeared on May 2nd and 11th. When the county government sent people to comfort them, they often knelt down and cried for help. The situation in other counties is also generally the same, so I will not elaborate. As for the authorities' response, in addition to the county magistrates and local gentry temporarily raising food, distributing it by name, and persuading them to return home, they also telegraphed the province to request relief. The Liaoning provincial government had previously proposed allocating funds to help spring plowing, but in reality, it did not have any effect. (May 15th)

Jiangsu Higher Qualification Examination Results Announced

Three Passed All Subjects

The examination papers have been graded and the results were announced by the Examination Committee yesterday, the 19th. Three candidates passed all subjects and their names were immediately posted for notification. The certificates of qualification will be issued at a later date according to the unified method prescribed by the Examination Committee. The certificates of passing for each subject will also be issued at a later date according to the unified method prescribed by the Central Government. Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Meeting of the Security Corps Committee: The county government previously received orders from the province to organize security corps in various districts and appointed "clearing the countryside" (清鄉) inspectors to supervise in Songjiang. The county government convened a meeting to organize the Security Corps Committee and decided on the list of security corps in various districts, requiring them to be submitted by May 15th. Today (20th), the county government convened the Security Corps Committee to discuss funding and other issues. The attendees included the district head Zhong Taishi and more than a dozen appointed committee members such as Ni Bingshi. County Magistrate Jin presided over the meeting and discussed the issue that only a few districts had submitted the list of security corps within the time limit. It was decided to extend the deadline by half a month and strictly require all districts to submit the list as soon as possible for organization. As for the fundraising methods for the Security Corps funding, it was the general consensus that since the lists have not yet been submitted, it is impossible to estimate them for the time being. It was decided that a meeting should be convened again after the lists are submitted to decide.

Suzhou

Bandits Rob on the Road: Dai Bingnan, Deputy Director of the Jiangdu County Court Detention Center, was ordered to transfer to the Jiangning District Court Detention Center. After visiting his family in Changan Alley, Zhabei, Shanghai, he arrived in Suzhou on the 19th by train. He planned to visit Huang Jinming, a former colleague from the old Wu District Court, at No. 10 Tongren Street in the city, to travel to Beijing together to take up new positions. After getting off the train, he immediately hired Yin Rusong's rickshaw to enter the city. At the entrance of Tanggong Alley under Chongzhen Bridge in Dongzhong Market, more than a dozen hooligans suddenly rushed out from the tiger stove in the alleyway, dragged Dai out of the rickshaw, violently beat him, and robbed him. A total of 50 yuan in banknotes from the Bank of China, a piece of woolen fabric, and several other cosmetics were robbed from his bag. He still had 50 yuan on him, but because Dai shouted for help, the police on duty arrived and it was not taken. Afterwards, Dai reported to the 16th Precinct, and Inspector Xu Yubing led the police to the scene, arresting Zhou Liqiang, the owner of the tiger stove, and forcing him to lead the arrest of the robbers. At 2:00 AM that night, three principal offenders, Liu Afu, Zhang Laosan, and Liu Jinhai, were arrested at Zhang Laosan's house at No. 38 Tongren Street, along with six suspects: Ju Fulong, Lü Liubao, Zhang Liansheng, Chen Jinrong, Chen A'jin, and Liu Renshui. All were taken to the station. During interrogation, Liu Afu and others confessed to colluding with Zhang Laosan, Liu Jinhai, and Wang Xiaowu (who is still at large) to rob pedestrians. However, they denied robbing the 50 yuan in banknotes. After the interrogation, they were transferred to the branch bureau for further investigation at 4:00 AM yesterday (the 20th).

Appeal Hearing for the Murder of Wife Case: Hu Yinglong, an employee of the Songjiang Dianye Bank, was accused by his wife's younger brothers, Zhang Zeqian and Zhang Zexu, in the Songjiang County Court of conspiring with his stepmother, Hu Nie, to murder his wife, Zhang Wenrui. The Songjiang County Court acquitted Hu Yinglong and Hu Nie on March 30 of this year. However, the prosecutor of the Songjiang County Court appealed to the High Court, and the remains were sent to Suzhou along with the case file. Yesterday (the 20th), Zhan Yufen, the presiding judge of the Third Criminal Division, held a hearing, summoning the deceased's brothers, Zhang Zeqian and Zhang Zexu, to testify. Hu Yinglong and Hu Nie hired lawyers Sun Yuan and Zhang Baopei to defend them. Hu Yinglong testified first, stating that he was 32 years old, a native of Songjiang, and worked in the banking business. In February of the 17th year of the Republic of China, he married Zhang Wenrui. They were usually on good terms. On the seventh day of the seventh month of the lunar calendar last year, his wife asked him for money, and they had an argument. In the middle of the night, she hanged herself on the bed railing. He immediately took her down and reported the news to the Zhang family on the eighth day. The two Zhang Zeqian brothers also came to help with the funeral arrangements. They accused him of strangling his wife, but that was not the case. Hu Nie testified that she was 43 years old, and Yinglong was her nephew. He and his wife had always been on good terms. She didn't know about their argument on the seventh day of the seventh month last year. On the morning of the eighth day, her nephew told her that Hu Zhang had hanged herself. She went to his room, but the body had already been taken down. She did not go to the autopsy. They accused her of helping to murder Hu Zhang, but that was not the case. Zhang Zeqian testified that he was 26 years old, from outside the West Gate of Songjiang, and worked as a pawnbroker. Zhang Wenrui was his older sister. On the morning of the eighth day of the seventh month last year, Hu Yinglong first sent someone to report that his sister was suffering from acute cholera. Less than five minutes later, another messenger came to report that she was dead. He and his younger brother Zexu went to the Hu family together. When they arrived at his sister's room, the body was on the bed, with her eyes half-closed. He immediately suspected Hu Yinglong's uncles, Hu Runzhang and Hu Runde, who told them not to get close to the body, because his sister died of an epidemic and they feared it would be contagious. Hu Runzhang then asked him to write a funeral announcement. On the ninth day, the coffin was sealed and the funeral procession returned to the Hu family. They asked Hu Yinglong about the cause of his sister's death. Hu Yinglong said she had hanged herself. Later, they became more suspicious, and on the eleventh day of that month, they reported to the Songjiang County Court, requesting them to send someone to examine the body. On the twelfth day, Prosecutor Luo supervised the opening of the coffin. The examination revealed that the deceased had indeed been strangled to death by someone before her death. Prosecutor Luo then compared Hu Yinglong's hand to the wound, and it matched very well. Therefore, they accused him of murder, etc. Zhang Zexu testified that he was 24 years old and worked in the grain business. After his sister married Hu Yinglong, their relationship was just so-so. After receiving news of his sister's death from the Hu family, he went with his brother. At the time, he saw marks on his sister's throat. He wanted to report it to the Songjiang County Court to request an examination, but Hu Runzhang and Hu Runde dissuaded him. They accused him of murder because they reported that she died of a sudden illness. He asked them to produce a doctor's diagnosis, but they could not. Later, they requested an examination, and Prosecutor Luo determined that the deceased had indeed been strangled to death. He also requested the presiding judge to review Hu Yinglong's confession in the first instance, which included the statement, "I don't get along with Hu Zhang, but I get along with Hu Nie. Why do I get along with Hu Nie? Because Hu Nie doesn't allow me to get along with Hu Zhang." This shows that Hu Zhang's death was undoubtedly a conspiracy between Hu Yinglong and Hu Nie. After hearing the testimony, Judge Zhan stated that the case still required investigation of evidence and that the coroner who conducted the examination needed to be summoned to testify before another hearing and debate could be held.

Military Police Shoot and Kill Bandit: At 11:00 PM on the 19th, four bandits were on the roof of a house in Waikuatang Town, using a flashlight to look down. A member of the defense corps spotted them and immediately reported to the night-duty corps member, who set out to search and arrest them. At the same time, Zhao Wancheng, the platoon leader of the 6th company of the 1st regiment of stationed military police, also heard the alarm and led his troops to surround and arrest them. The defense corps climbed onto the roof to pursue them. Three bandits escaped by jumping off the roof, while one bandit ran around on the roof, crossing more than a dozen houses. He jumped off the roof into the river to escape, but was shot and killed in the river by the military police. Later, a bandit boat was found in the river, along with a bandit woman, Zhang Xu, who confessed that the deceased was her lover, named Zhang Shaoliang. Yesterday morning (the 20th), she was sent to the Weiting 11th Public Security Branch for verification and reported to the local court for examination of the corpse.

Wuxi

Tragic News of Parents Killing Their Own Child: Gong Hongbao, a resident of Yuhang Street, Xidiao Bridge, outside the West Gate of this county (a 25-year-old native of Jiangyin), opened a clothing store there, and his business was doing well. Five years ago, he had an affair with a 47-year-old woman, Jiang Chen. They were intimate and acted like husband and wife. In a few years, they had a son named A'gen (3 years old this year). After the birth, Jiang Chen, due to her old age, had no milk, so she sent the child to the countryside to be raised. Last autumn, she brought him back to raise herself. Unexpectedly, after the child was brought back, he cried incessantly all day long, which angered Gong Hongbao and his wife. On the night before yesterday, they used a sewing needle to stab dozens of needles into the child's face, causing blood to flow like a stream and his breathing to weaken. He died yesterday, which is truly tragic. The neighbors learned of the incident and, feeling indignant, came forward to negotiate with Gong, advocating reporting to the authorities for investigation.

Two Hostages Released from Fenshuidun: It is learned that in Fenshuidun Town, at the border of Xiwuyi, a large gang of more than 30 bandits entered the town and robbed and kidnapped five men and women as hostages some days ago. It is now known that Wu Runfu, the eldest son of Wu Peida, the owner of the kidnapped hotel, and Zhang Jinhai, a shop assistant, were released from the bandit den yesterday after a plan was devised. Wang Wenlin, Liu Shi, and her daughter, however, remain in the bandit den awaiting ransom.

Changshu

Kunzhi Ferry Overturns Cargo Ship: Yutai Clothing Store, located in Xiaodongmen of this county, has a strong capital base. Every year, it must send personnel to Shen Su Xikun and other places to buy old goods in pawnshops. On the 13th of this month, Wang Xianting, the manager of the store, and several partners went to Kunshan Baoyuan Pawnshop to buy goods worth more than 7,800 taels of silver, packed into 17 large packages. They hired a civilian boat and loaded it on the 18th to transport it to Changshu, entrusting a clerk, Gao Deyuan, to escort the load. Because it was inconvenient to row the boat, it was hooked to an inland river ferry, the Jia'e, traveling between Changshu and Qingyang Port, to be towed. Unexpectedly, when traveling in Kuncheng Lake, the wind was quite strong and the waves were very rapid. At that time, a Kunzhi Ban (Kunshan to Zhitang) ferry, the Jia'e, was sailing and suddenly wanted to overtake the boat in front without sounding its whistle, causing the Yutai Clothing Store's cargo ship to be overturned. The clothes and packages placed in the ship were all overturned into the river. The ferry immediately stopped and tried to salvage the clothes and packages. The clothes inside were all soaked in water, especially the fine fur goods, which suffered the greatest loss. The manager of the store is now directly negotiating with the Changqing Bureau, requesting compensation.

Defense Corps Seizes Large Number of Bandits: The Nansha District of this county is located on the coast, and bandit cases have occurred frequently and are difficult to solve. It is now learned that among the bandits, due to a dispute over the issue of snatching a wife, internal strife occurred. One of the bandits, Guan Guihou, a native of Fuxing Town, recently married a new wife, bought from a certain Tang for 80 yuan overseas. The woman's beauty moved the bandit leader Liu Shiyuan, who planned to take her for himself. At the same time, another bandit also planned to make a move, but he had no money, so he held a grudge and went to report it to the defense corps for arrest. Unexpectedly, Guan had already heard the news and escaped first, only capturing one accomplice, Zhou Yuanhou. Zhou San then revealed the locations of the various bandits in his confession, which were within the territory of Nantong. He then joined forces with the Tong Defense Corps and successively arrested Zhou Jin and Liu Yuegen in Fuxing Town. Later, Xue Laoer and Qian Guotai were arrested in Youche Port. When arresting the Qian bandit, Qian Pinlan, the captain of the Fourth District Defense Corps, stepped forward to knock on the door. Unexpectedly, many people rushed out from inside and opened fire to resist arrest. Qian was shot and immediately fainted. The corps members also opened fire in retaliation. The two sides fought fiercely for two hours before the bandits were unable to hold out and retreated. Captain Qian has now gone to the Shazhou City Hospital for treatment. The bandits are all temporarily detained at the corps headquarters.

Changzhou

Nine Bandits Executed by Firing Squad: Zhang Pengzhu, the county magistrate and director of the Qingxiang Bureau of Wujin County, previously obtained the surrender of nine bandits, Yu Rongda, Zou Rongchun, Zhou Gengsheng, Zhu Jinkun, Chen Yinxi, Wu Sanlin, Tu Liuguan, and Zhang Wuda. After questioning them separately, they confessed to the crimes. They were sentenced to death and reported to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for approval of execution by firing squad. Zhang, who was also the director, sent police to Lanqian at 7:00 AM today (the 20th) to extract Yu Rongda and the other nine bandits, verified their identities, and tied them to the Fengweidun execution ground for execution by firing squad.

Yangzhou

Bandits Burn Victim: In the Fangjia Village area of ​​Situ Temple Fort in Yishus, there is a person named Chou Yongkang, whose family runs a mill and the business is quite prosperous, thus arousing the covetousness of bandits. Around 2 AM the night before, more than 20 bandits suddenly came and rushed into the house, each holding a handgun, demanding money from Chou. Chou replied that he had no money. The bandits were furious and searched again and again, but found nothing. They then pressed Chou to the ground and burned his back with straw, causing burns in several places. Later, the bandits, because it was about to dawn, did not dare to linger for a long time, so they limited Chou to raising 500 yuan within four days, and agreed to pay the money at Saogou Mountain outside the West Gate, using a lamp as a signal. After speaking, they roared and left. Chou's injuries are now quite serious, and he has already been taken to the city for treatment.

Nantong

Preparing to Organize Coastal Patrol Team: From Lüsi to the Sheyang River estuary in Yancheng, Jiangbei, the coastal shoals are continuous and have not yet been included in the military police area. Now that the fishing protection and bandit suppression affairs have ended, but the escaped and defeated bandits, after the fleet leaves, it is difficult to guarantee that they will not come back to cause trouble. The provincial military and political authorities have decided that each coastal county should gather and prepare to organize a coastal patrol team, equipped with ten motor gunboats to specialize in patrolling and suppressing fleeing bandits. It will be established in the shortest possible time.

Eleventh Division Injured Soldiers Factory to Move Elsewhere: All circles in Tongchang opposed the Eleventh Division stationed in Hankou setting up an injured soldiers factory in Tong, and the representatives sent to Nanjing to petition are discussing with Commander Chen Cheng. On the 19th, a telegram arrived in Tong, stating that Minister He of the Ministry of Military Affairs had agreed to instruct the division to choose another location to move to. The pauper's workshop will still be established by the local government as a vagrant training center.

County Government Takes Over Qingxiang Bureau: The Nantong Qingxiang Bureau was ordered to be abolished, and the 32 prisoners and documents and maps were taken over by the county government on the 19th.

Rugao

Department Order to Seize Ji Dunchuo's Property: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, because Ji Dunchuo, the former ninth district chief of Rugao County, had illegally acted as a grass-roots administrator, arbitrarily executing bandits and embezzling public funds. The department had previously submitted a report to the provincial government, ordering his dismissal and returning to the case for investigation. However, Li has not yet reported to the case. Now, the department has ordered the Rugao County Government to ascertain all the property of Ji Dunchuo in the district and to pre-emptively seize it in accordance with judicial procedures for future compensation for the embezzled funds. After receiving the order, the county government is said to have complied with it.

Hangzhou

Arch Quay Fire Kills Two: The house of Wu Demao, behind the Ersi Temple in Arch Quay, caught fire the night before due to careless cocoon baking, causing a great fire. Fortunately, the local gangs gathered and tried their best to put out the fire, which was extinguished only after it had burned down 27 thatched sheds. Wu's great-grandmother-in-law (70 years old) and Wu's wife's sister-in-law both died in the fire because they could not escape. It is truly tragic.

Xiaoshan

Mountain Boundary Dispute Leads to Murder: In the Zhengjiawu area along Xiang Lake outside the West Gate of Xiaoshan, a farmer named Zheng Jinhuai recently purchased several acres of mountain land. Unexpectedly, a certain Shan and others from Laisuxiang outside the East Gate claimed it was public property, abruptly making things difficult and forcing him to return the boundary. Because Zheng was forced to do so, he hanged himself from a tree on the mountain on the 15th. The next day, his family found him and thought he had been strangled, so they petitioned the court on the 17th for an examination and ordered a strict arrest of the murderer. It is unknown how a murder case will end.

Crowding the Bridal Chamber Injures Several People: Chen Jiyuan, a resident of Xiwang, Xiaoshan, married off his son on the 16th. While they were sending her into the bridal chamber, because a general group of well-wishers were fighting to see the bride, there were too many people, and the building suddenly collapsed. All the bride, groom, and well-wishers fell into a pile. Underneath was the kitchen stove. At the time, the pots, bowls, and utensils were all broken. The groom suffered serious head and chest injuries, and two well-wishers had broken legs and were also in danger. There was also an old woman who was cooking downstairs who had been crushed to the point of almost dying, and there was fear for her life.

Taizhou

Change of County Magistrates in Linhuang: Hou Changling, the magistrate of Linhai County, has been approved to resign. Xu Shixian (from Yuyao) has been appointed to fill the vacancy. Sun Chongxia, the magistrate of Huangyan County, has also been approved to resign. Jiang Huizhao (from Xiuning, Anhui) has been appointed to fill the vacancy.

Department Sends Delegates to Linhai to Eradicate Opium Seedlings: The Zhejiang Department of Civil Affairs has dispatched Yu Cheng from Xianju to Linhai to discuss opium eradication matters with Yang Gonghong, the acting county magistrate of this county. Today (the 18th), he met with Meng Xian, the director of the county Public Security Bureau, and led a large team of military police to eradicate opium in the eastern townships first.

Education News Highlights

Exhaustion of Education Funds in Jiangsu Province

Recent Expenditure Situation of the Department of Education

丨Middle Schools and Rural Normal Schools Paid Up to March丨

丨Experimental Primary Schools Paid Up to April丨

The Jiangsu Department of Education, recognizing that the recurring expenses of various educational institutions in the province were in arrears for several months, making it difficult to maintain operations, urgently needed to find ways to provide relief. In addition to constantly consulting with the management office to find ways to raise funds, it also submitted a request to the provincial government on May 12, ordering the Department of Finance to clear all the provincial treasury subsidies for this year within a set period to facilitate turnover, and also wrote to the management office to find ways to borrow to meet urgent needs. It is now known that up to recently, the expenses of various provincial middle schools and social education institutions have been paid up to the first half of March, the expenses of middle schools and rural normal schools have been paid up to the second half of March, and the expenses of various experimental primary schools have been paid up to the first half of April.

Document from the Jiangsu Department of Education to the Provincial Government

Document No. 216 from the Jiangsu Department of Education to the Provincial Government states: Case investigation: The provincial treasury subsidized 300,000 yuan for provincial education expenses in the 19th year. The committee meeting of your government previously decided to include it in the local budget of the 19th year, and it was also decided to divide it into twelve months and allocate it monthly on average, ordering the Department of Finance to comply with the record. Now, there are only a little over a month left before the end of the year, and this subsidy for rural expenses has been in huge arrears due to the provincial treasury's financial difficulties. At this time of weak tax revenue, the education expenses management office has exhausted all its resources, and the recurring expenses of various educational institutions have only been paid up to the first half of February, except for the half month of March that has been paid to various experimental primary schools. Various institutions have been in arrears of funds for a long time, are in dire straits, find it difficult to maintain operations, and have submitted petitions for relief one after another to avoid difficulties. It has been found that the above-mentioned provincial treasury subsidy funds have long been included in the budget and are earmarked for specific purposes. It is clear that the current provincial treasury is in financial difficulties and it is difficult to cope. However, considering that various educational institutions are eagerly awaiting funds, if ways are not found to provide relief, the impact on the future of education will be profound. Therefore, this document is prepared and submitted to your government for review. It is earnestly hoped that the Department of Finance will be ordered to find ways to allocate the unpaid subsidies for this year in full within a set period to facilitate turnover and meet urgent needs. This is in the public interest. Respectfully submitted, Chairman Ye of the Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee, Chen Hexian, Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education.

Letter from the Department of Education to the Education Expenses Management Office

Public Letter No. 310 from the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education states: Case According to various provincial schools and educational institutions, the recurring expenses have been in arrears for a long time, making it difficult to maintain operations, and requesting relief, etc. Based on this, it is found that this year's education expenses have been affected by the previous year's famine. Although the actual income and expenditure in the budget are not significantly different, the expenditure has been exhausted, and the recurring expenses have been in arrears for many months. It is true that it is difficult for your office to allocate funds due to the emptiness of the treasury. Various educational institutions are in dire straits, awaiting funds to maintain operations, which is also the real situation. Relief should be urgently sought to maintain operations. The above-mentioned situation is hereby reported. Please check and consider doing your best to find ways to allocate funds, or still follow the old practice of previous years, find ways to borrow to temporarily maintain operations, and hope to see a reply. Chen Hexian, to the Jiangsu Education Expenses Management Office.

Letter from the Education Expenses Management Office to the Committee

Letter from the Jiangsu Education Management Fee Office to the Education Expenses Committee states: Direct Startup: Previously, due to the letter from the joint meeting of teachers and staff of secondary schools urging the issuance of cleared accumulated expenses, the Committee was requested by letter to quickly convene a meeting to strive for relief methods in the record. Now, I have received another letter from the school representative of secondary schools, saying: Direct Startup: School expenses have been in arrears for three months, the mountains are exhausted, and it is difficult to maintain. Colleagues gathered and discussed at Zhenjiang Middle School on the 30th of last month. Everyone said that the noble office is in charge of education expenses, and is responsible for collecting, paying and issuing. If one is in charge of arrears and ignores it, trapping the school in a desperate situation, what will happen to guilt? Er is consistent in the decision, please give priority to this month by the 25th, and issue the arrears before April, otherwise colleagues will not be responsible, but from June 1st, the advance leave is forced, the situation is forced, it is really impossible. The noble office should not sit back and ignore it, etc. Except for a letter reply, the corresponding is another Feng Da, that is, Xi Chazhao, and quickly meeting the rescue method, I can't wait for the order, this is the Jiangsu Education Expenses Committee, Su Education Management Office replied to the representatives of the principals of middle schools, saying: Straight resumption: Jiezhan's big letter, Bei Renyi is also one of them. In view of the fact that the Beidi Office previously prepared and issued the regular expenses of each school, Yan urged the counties to pay the tax money within the time limit, in order to gradually allocate and clear the arrears of each school, the tax revenue of each item, and the present value of the light month. The Suzhou Women's Athletic Meet to Be Held the Day After Tomorrow

Yesterday's Baseball Preliminaries: Girls' Vocational School Wins Over Huiling

Cheng Lie's Preliminary Results Are Excellent

丨50-Meter Long Jump Breaks National Record丨

The Suzhou Women's Athletic Federation, since its establishment, has reached two years. Last year, the first sports meeting was held at Soochow University in Tianci Zhuang, and the championship was won by Suzhou Women's Middle School. This year it is scheduled to be held on the 23rd of this month at the athletic field of Cheng Lie Physical Education College in Zhujiazhuang. The Cheng Lie Women's Department held preliminary elections on the afternoon of the 19th. Zhuang Mingzhen's 50-meter and long jump both broke the national record. The 50-meter was 7.2 seconds, breaking Sun Guiyun's 7.4 seconds. The long jump was 4.55 meters, breaking the latest national new record of 4.49 meters set by Li Bojin of Beiping. In addition, Zhu Peiqiong of the school achieved a long jump result of 4.52 meters, also breaking the national record. Therefore, this year's championship will be highly competitive.

In addition, a baseball competition has been added to this year's games, with participation from Huiling, Girls' Vocational School, Jinghai, and Le Yi schools. Yesterday afternoon at 3:30, Huiling and Girls' Vocational School held preliminary elections at the playground of the former site of the Le Yi Girls' Middle School in Huangfeiji, with Zhu Songsun and Zhang Nianzu serving as referees. As a result, the Girls' Vocational School won with a score of 39 to 18. Today in the afternoon, Jinghai and Le Yi will still hold preliminary elections at the original location. The winners will hold the finals in the sports meet the day after tomorrow.

Local News

Tu Weizeng Discusses the Sino-Soviet Conference

Currently Discussing the Railway Redemption Issue

Ordered to Collect Materials in Beijing

Mr. Tu Weizeng, a special commissioner for the Sino-Soviet Conference, was ordered to return to Beijing to report on the progress of the negotiations. He arrived in Shanghai the other day. A reporter made a special visit to inquire about the latest developments of the Sino-Soviet Conference and the economic situation of Soviet Russia. According to him, he and Special Commissioner Wang Zeng'en arrived in Harbin on April 24th. After a brief stay, they took the land route to Beijing. After arriving in Beijing, they repeatedly met with Foreign Minister Wang and Vice Minister Wang to report on the progress of the negotiations. On the one hand, they were ordered by Representative Mo to collect reference materials from the railway and foreign affairs departments. It seems that when Representative Mo was in Beijing last time, he collected a lot of materials and personally took them to Russia for reference, but due to the urgency of time, they were not complete enough. Therefore, this time, taking advantage of the opportunity, he ordered Tu Weizeng and Wang Zeng'en to find ways to supplement them and take them with them for use. As for the Sino-Soviet Conference, the first formal meeting was held on April 11th. Our side immediately put forward the outline for railway redemption, and the other side also put forward a counter-proposal. At the second and third meetings, discussions on this proposal began and are currently ongoing. As for the issues of commerce and resumption of diplomatic relations, they have not yet been mentioned. In short, if the Russian side has sincerity, it will not be difficult to resolve the matter satisfactorily. Whether or not Russia has sincerity depends on the domestic political situation. Regarding the economic situation of Soviet Russia, because it is currently the time to implement the Five-Year Economic Plan, all parties are tightening their belts and striving to implement it. Regardless of its ideology, its spirit and perseverance are worthy of emulation. He will return to Beijing within a few days to sort out the collected materials and plans to go north to Russia in early June. The newly appointed special commissioner Xu Jianping will not go to Russia for the time being.

Madame Zhang Xueliang, Yu Fengzhi, Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Seeking Medical Treatment in Shanghai, Returning to Beijing Tonight

Madame Yu Fengzhi, wife of Deputy Commander Zhang, along with her secretary and attendants, arrived in Shanghai by express train from Beijing the night before last. At 6:35 yesterday morning, she arrived at the North Station and drove to the Cangzhou Hotel to rest. She is scheduled to return to Beijing tonight. The details are as follows:

Station Welcome: Yesterday morning, the area near the North Station was protected by armed police officers dispatched by the Public Security Bureau, as well as detectives from the Garrison Headquarters and Chinese and Western detectives from the Public Works Department, who were on standby on the platform. The military band of the Public Security Bureau also arrived at the station to play music to welcome her. Those who went to the North Station to welcome her included Zhou Xiangxian, a counselor from the Ministry of Finance, Tang Liu, the director of the Foreign Affairs Office, Zhao Tiezhang, the section chief, Jiang Yi, the chief of the adjutant office of the Garrison Headquarters, Shen Nengyi, the director of the Printing Bureau of the Ministry of Finance, and Qian Jiechen, among others, totaling more than ten people.

Resting at Cangzhou: At 6:35 yesterday morning, the train entered the North Station. Madame Yu's private carriage was attached to the last car. Those who came to welcome her rushed to meet her. Madame Yu, wearing a short black velvet coat and a light-colored cheongsam, stepped slowly out of the car. Amidst the military music, she walked out of the platform and took a special No. 7777 car prepared by Mr. Du Yuesheng and went straight to the Cangzhou Hotel. At that time, Madame Song Ailing, the wife of Kong Xiangxi, arrived at the Cangzhou Hotel by car to greet her and met her at the entrance, and hand in hand they went inside to rest.

Accompanying Figures: Those who accompanied her included Wu Jingan, the director of the Siping-Taonan Railway Bureau, Miss Zhu Si, Wu's wife, Li Yingchao, Deputy Commander Zhang's secretary, the secretary of Miss Darnell, the American advisor to the Deputy Commander's office, and nine guards.

Kong Residence Banquet: Madame Yu and others rested briefly at Cangzhou, and then traveled in the same car with Madame Kong to the Kong residence on Avenue Haig. A doctor from the Shanghai Sanitarium and Hospital was called to the Kong residence to treat Madame Yu's ailment. A banquet was held at the Kong residence at noon to welcome her. In the afternoon, she went to major companies to purchase miscellaneous items. In the evening, she attended a banquet hosted by Madame Song, the old lady, on Seymour Road. After dinner, she went to the Grand Theatre to watch a play.

Zhang Has Arrived in Tianjin: Last night, Mr. Shen Nengyi received a telegram from Tianjin, asking to be forwarded to the Deputy Commander's wife: "The Deputy Commander, along with his two sons and attendants, arrived safely in Tianjin at 2:10 p.m. today." Therefore, Madame Yu urgently needs to return to the north and has decided to take the night train at 11:45 tonight back to Beijing and then take the Jinpu Railway north.

American Congressmen to Visit Shanghai

A Group of Five in Total

Arrival Expected on June 2nd

According to the "North-China Daily News", the American Commercial Counselor received a telegram from his country yesterday stating that three American senators and two members of the House of Representatives, who are coming to China to investigate the silver issue, will arrive in Shanghai at the beginning of next month. Senator Pittman will be on the President Jefferson ship and is expected to arrive in Shanghai on June 2nd. It is estimated that they will stay in China for about a month. Senator Oddie and his wife, niece, and son, Senator Robinson, Representative Deyer and his wife, Representative Gilbert and his daughter, etc., all departed from San Francisco on the American transport ship USS Chaumont on April 23rd. They will first go to the Philippine Islands and then come to China. They will also arrive in Shanghai on June 2nd. They plan to travel to North China and then return to Shanghai, passing through Manila, and returning to San Francisco on July 24th. Furthermore, retired U.S. Navy Vice Admiral Clark will also come to Shanghai from Manila on the same ship. U.S. Navy Vice Admiral Hienton will come to Shanghai from the United States on the President Hayes. The American Chamber of Commerce in this city is currently preparing to welcome them.

Closure of the Sand and Gravel Industry

Successful Petition Results

Following the unanimous closure of the sand and gravel industry in the city due to opposition to the provincial government's increased levies, representatives petitioned various authorities yesterday. The results were very satisfactory. The Ministry of Finance has also issued instructions to investigate and cancel the levy. The details of yesterday's events are recorded below:

Sand and Gravel Industry Meeting The Sand and Gravel Trade Association held a meeting the previous evening (the 19th) at 7:00 PM to discuss the issue of the closure and devise countermeasures. More than 300 members attended. The chairman, Lu Xiaozuo, resolved the following items: (1) The industry-wide closure is a major issue, with implications for local stability. Representatives should be dispatched to various locations to actively dissuade [from adding additional levies]. Simultaneously, documents should be prepared by Lu Xiaozuo and Wu Longhai to report to the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Bureau of Social Affairs, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting them to take measures to address the issue. (2) A notice should be published in the newspaper to encourage members of the association to resume business immediately. (3) The objectives of the petition are: (A) To request the prohibition of the collection of the onerous tax imposed by Da Chang and Yi Tai, which is similar to a disguised likin, with a newly added management fee of seven coppers per ton, within Jiangsu Province. (B) To request a submission to the Zhejiang Provincial Government to immediately revoke it. (4) To submit a request to the National Government's Ministry of Finance and the municipal party and government organs, stating the reasons and requesting the cancellation of the management fee.

The Situation of the Petition Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, the Sand and Gravel Trade Association dispatched representatives Lu Xiaozuo, Wu Longhai, Ye Zhen, Gong Bin, and others, six people in total, along with a petition letter, to the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, and the Bureau of Social Affairs. As a result, the authorities agreed to forward the request to the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Construction to cancel the increased levies and advised the representatives to resume business first and await a resolution. The representatives were satisfied and withdrew.

Ministry of Finance Instructions The Ministry of Finance instructed the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating, "Received a telegram, stating that the Sand and Gravel Trade Association of this city has submitted a letter to the Zhejiang Department of Construction regarding the collection of sand and mud production and sales taxes. The situation is presented and a request is made for cancellation." The instructions read, "The telegram has been received. A consultation will be sent to the Zhejiang Provincial Government to investigate and cancel the tax. Please comply accordingly."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Submission The Municipal Chamber of Commerce further submitted a document to the Ministry of Finance and the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, stating, "Submitting [this] concerning contractors extorting sand and mud taxes, leading to a shutdown of business, requesting examination and approval, and swift orders to exempt [the tax] in order to stabilize business affairs." This was regarding a case on the 20th of this month, based on a letter from the Shanghai Sand and Gravel Trade Association (the original letter appeared in yesterday's newspaper). Upon investigation, it was found that on May 4th, the association had previously stated that the Zhejiang Province's contracted collection of sand and mud production tax was essentially a disguised likin. A telegram was sent to the Ministry of Finance requesting an order to cease the collection. Subsequently, on the 19th of this month, a response was received under the reference number [number], stating that a consultation would be sent to the Zhejiang Provincial Government to investigate and cancel the tax, and compliance was requested. The contractors responsible for collecting this sand and mud levy should immediately comply with the order to cease collection. However, the two tax collection companies, Da Chang and Yi Tai, are using high-pressure tactics, detaining goods and people, leading to an industry-wide shutdown. At a time when likin is being vigorously abolished, this illegal extortion is occurring. If this is not strictly rectified, where will government orders be placed? It is appropriate to submit the situation to your ministry and bureau for review, promptly issue a strict order to cease collection, and find ways to alleviate the situation, thereby stabilizing commerce. This is for the public good." This was respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Finance and the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs.

Investigation by the Public Works Department The Public Works Department of the Public Concession sent a special commissioner to the Sand and Gravel Trade Association yesterday to investigate the situation due to the sand and gravel shutdown, which could affect municipal construction projects, in order to find ways to remedy the situation.

Declaration by the Construction Industry The Construction Industry Association believes that the sand and gravel shutdown is greatly related to construction projects in the construction industry. If it is not resolved soon, construction projects will inevitably be suspended. Therefore, it issued a notice yesterday, scheduling a meeting on the 23rd (Saturday) afternoon to discuss countermeasures and inviting the sand and gravel industry to participate.

Slaughter Shutdown by Concession Butchers

Bureau of Finance Requests Municipal Chamber of Commerce to Persuade [Them] to Resume Business

The fresh meat industry in this city has been closed for six days due to the slaughter tax issue. Butchers in the Public Concession took unified action yesterday, and the French Concession side has also confirmed a slaughter shutdown today. The various situations obtained yesterday are recorded below:

Slaughter Shutdown in the Concessions More than 300 shops, including Lu Gaojian and other fresh meat businesses in the Public Concession, have uniformly stopped importing goods and are implementing a shutdown starting yesterday in order to assist fellow businesses in the northern and southern parts of the city. As a result, the Juxing Slaughterhouse on Yuezhou Road, the Renyuan Slaughterhouse on Jiaxing Road, and the Ninghai Slaughterhouse on Dawang Temple Road have already ceased slaughtering yesterday. However, the Public Works Department Slaughterhouse on Huasheng Road and the Suxi Slaughterhouse on Dawang Temple Road will cease slaughtering today due to existing pigs. More than 300 shops, including Fang Yongda and other fresh meat businesses in the French Concession, have confirmed that they will stop importing goods and implement a shutdown today. As a result, the Public Works Department Slaughterhouse on Nanyang Bridge will also cease slaughtering. The association sent letters to the Public Works Department of the Public Concession and the French Concession Public Works Department yesterday, requesting protection.

Municipal Government Directive The Municipal Government issued a directive to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating, "Based on a report requesting that the municipal slaughter tax continue to be paid according to the original assessed amount, and requesting the cancellation of pre-slaughter and post-slaughter inspection fees," and "The two reports have been noted. The municipal slaughter tax has been collected for a long time in the past. Recently, this government approved a request from the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office to collect and remit [the tax] on its behalf, and the collection of the new tax did not increase the tax rate. The cancellation of contractors and direct collection was originally intended to streamline tax regulations, simplify collection procedures, and provide convenience to merchants and the public without causing harassment. Furthermore, the tax rate is different from the tax amount. This government is collecting according to the originally set tax rate, which is in accordance with the methods set by the ministry. The statement in the report that [this] violates [the regulations] is a misunderstanding. As for the pre-slaughter and post-slaughter inspection fees, these are hygiene procedure fees, not taxes. The request for approval is difficult to grant. Please inform [them] accordingly."

Bureau of Finance Reply The Municipal Bureau of Finance replied to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating, "Responding directly to your association's Public Letter No. 88, regarding the resolution passed by the Fresh Meat Industry Association of this city, requesting the cancellation of the slaughter tax and the conversion to a business tax, and the uniform cancellation of the pre-slaughter fee in the concessions, the post-slaughter fee in the interior, and the inspection fee for technicians in the four rural areas. Furthermore, if the municipal government's plan to build a new slaughterhouse is implemented, the industry will feel inconvenienced and requests the revocation of the order, with the industry continuing to operate in separate districts. In addition, the municipal government's purchase of tickets for tax collection was extended to the 15th. After the expiration date, please do not force the purchase of tickets again. Before the business tax is changed, the industry will continue to pay the original assessed amount." The reply stated, "Upon approval, the tax collection by contractors easily leads to the abuses of control and monopoly, and the legitimate tax revenue is often misappropriated, which has long been criticized by society. As your letter states, the abolition of the contractor system is a proper measure in terms of tax system theory. Moreover, under a revolutionary government, efforts should be made to eliminate it as much as possible in order to comply with the tax system. This bureau was ordered to take over the slaughter tax and collect it directly in accordance with the original tax rate, without increasing any burden on the meat merchants. Reading the interview with Mr. Zheng Chengqing, the general manager of your association, published on the 17th of this month, [he] stated that the municipal slaughter tax has always been paid by the industry association. In the southern city, it is 3.9 coppers per pig, and the remaining amount is allocated to charitable causes. In Zhabei and rural areas, it is borne proportionally by the industry." This proves that this bureau's collection by counting heads is not an innovation, and the tax amount collected is not arbitrarily set. As for the proportional burden in Zhabei and rural areas, regardless of how it was proportionally allocated during the commercial operation era and whether the method was fair, just in the southern city, the tax rate is different from the northern city, and the burden on the citizens is inevitably uneven, and the tax rate lacks standards and violates the principles of taxation. Now that it has been taken back for self-operation, how can fairness be served if it is not collected by counting heads? If the contractors did allocate the remaining amount to charitable causes when they contracted to operate [the tax], the industry association may submit [a report] to the municipal government in the future to seek a remedy. As for continuing to pay the original assessed amount and following the old system of commercial operation, it is practically impossible to do so. In addition to reporting to the municipal government, a corresponding reply is sent, and you are still requested to investigate the original intention of the letter of May 9th of this year and earnestly persuade [them] to resume business quickly, without being foolishly misled and causing losses to themselves." This was addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce.

Chamber of Commerce Opinion A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency interviewed Mr. Wang Xiaolai, the chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, yesterday regarding the slaughter tax issue and asked for his opinion on the case. [Wang] replied, "The Chamber of Commerce has always taken a mediating attitude to assist in resolving this case. In my opinion, the southern city actually collected 3.9 coppers in the past, while the northern city and rural areas were allocated according to the amount, averaging less than two coppers. Now, in order to unify the tax rate, the tax rates in the northern and southern cities should be statistically analyzed and a fair tax rate should be set, which would be fairer. Therefore, I recently advocated reducing the tax rate. On the one hand, the funds for charitable causes that the meat industry handled in the past should also be appropriately subsidized. Then, this case may be resolved. Fortunately, the business tax in this city will be launched soon, and it may be possible to set a temporary method as a transition."

Request from Pig Dealers The Fresh Pig Dealers Association stated that the shutdown of meat merchants has had an impact. Yesterday, they sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce requesting mediation to resolve the issue as soon as possible. The correspondence is recorded below: (1) The letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce stated, "Respectfully submitting, upon investigation, the Fresh Meat Industry Association requested to change the slaughter tax to a business tax, and the reasons are legitimate. However, the authorities failed to understand, causing a unanimous expression of closure. If it were not unavoidable, who would be willing to sacrifice? This kind of unavoidable suffering is clearly evident here. Fortunately, your association is mindful of the difficulties of merchants, advocates fairness, and is providing relief. [We] are extremely grateful. Furthermore, this association and the fresh meat industry are in the same boat, and [we] are even more concerned. [We] deeply fear that prolonged delays will trap the meat industry in a difficult situation. [We] dare to ask your association to make every effort to mediate in order to resolve the issue as soon as possible, and [we] cannot bear the hope that the merchants of Suzhou will be out of trouble." (2) The Chamber of Commerce replied, "In reply, received your letter stating that the fresh meat industry requested to change the slaughter tax to a business tax, and the shutdown of business is an expression of the inevitable. Please mediate to resolve the issue." Upon investigation, this association has previously submitted the difficulties of the fresh meat industry to the Municipal Government and the Bureau of Finance, requesting leniency and adoption. Replies have been received and forwarded separately. Now, based on the letter, [we] will wait for the opportunity to mediate. If there is room for mediation, [we] will do our best. This letter is sent for your information.

The discussion lasted for a long time, and [he] left at 11:40 AM.

Restrictions on Political Gatherings in the French Concession

Permission from the French Chief Patrol is Required First

The French Chief Patrol has found that there have been unauthorized gatherings in violation of the regulations of this concession recently. He has re-promulgated the warning of the French Consul General's decision in Article 13 of the organizational charter of the French Concession Public Works Bureau on May 3, 1927, and notified the detective office of the special agency's political department to various groups. The original text is excerpted as follows: (1) Political gatherings, offices, joint meetings, or any groups may not be held or established in the French Concession without the permission of the French Consul General or his committee. (2) Anyone wishing to open a similar gathering, establish a similar office, form a similar joint meeting, or any group or individual, should submit an application to the French Chief Patrol for approval at least 48 hours in advance. The purpose of the gathering, the agenda of the meeting, the composition of the audience, and all details should be stated in the charter, or the purpose of the joint meeting or group should be reported, and the names of the responsible persons should be submitted. (3) This order repeals Order No. 6 of February 17, 1917.

Preliminary New Governance Project in Shanghai County

Tombs, etc., within the Land Enclosure

Must be Moved Before the 20th

The construction project of the new governance houses in Shanghai County was originally intended to be contracted by Dafang Construction Company. After consultation, it was decided that not following the bidding procedures would have many implications. Therefore, a fixed date of June 1 has been set for the commencement of commercial bidding. In addition, all obstacles such as tombs within the land enclosure for the new governance were originally limited to being moved out by the 20th of this month. Now, the county government sincerely fears that the time may be insufficient for the various businesses, so it has specially extended the deadline to the end of this month to clear the obstacles. Yesterday, the head of the third district, Yang, was instructed to inform the various businesses to comply. On one hand, the financial and construction bureaus will purchase another acre of land to prepare for the relocation of unclaimed coffins.

New Instruments of Weights and Measures Required by Various Industries

A Deadline Should Be Set for Reporting and Production

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various trade associations yesterday, stating, "In response to the promotion of the new system of weights and measures, we have sent a letter ordering the number of new instruments needed to be opened and sent to the meeting for compilation and forwarding. According to the reports from the soy sauce and seafood trade associations, a request has been submitted to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs for the record, and the Measurement and Testing Institute has sent a letter in response. The bureau's approval number is 10168, stating that the above has been noted. It is said that the Seafood Trade Association of this city has always used the British pound as the standard. Now that the new system of weights and measures is being promoted, the association should still be instructed to use kilograms or municipal catties for the British pound in order to comply with the law. The deadline for standardization is approaching. The association should again inform the various trade associations to quickly report the types of new instruments required by the deadline so that they can be forwarded for production." In view of the fact that the implementation of the new system of weights and measures is imminent, the types of new instruments that each association should use must be reported by the deadline. Please do not hesitate to wait and see. The above-mentioned causes have been notified by letter to be complied with.
