Record of the Tongji University Anniversary Celebration

Yesterday, the National Tongji University in Wusong held its 24th-anniversary celebration and the unveiling ceremony for Mr. Yuan Guanlan and Doctors Bao Long and Berentze. Details are recorded as follows:

Attendees: The meeting commenced at 10:00 AM yesterday. Attendees included figures from the medical and political/military circles of Shanghai, such as Tang Ying, President of Labor University; Shen Yi, Director of the Bureau of Public Works; Tian Sihan, President of the Agricultural School; Cheng Kuanzheng, Principal of Wusong Middle School; Yan Fuqing, President of Central University; Xu Peihuang, Director of the Municipal Bureau of Education; Ruan Jiepan, former President of Tongji University; Sun Kangzeng, President of the Merchant Marine School of the Ministry of Communications; Ma Lifan, Director of the Radio Administration of the Ministry of Communications; Yuan Xiluo; and other guests, totaling over a thousand people. The gathering was quite grand for the time. The three steles dedicated to Mr. Guanlan and the Doctors, with gold lettering on white stone, were erected in the middle of the walls on both sides of the auditorium.

Meeting Agenda: (1) Opening of the Meeting; (2) Everyone Stands at Attention; (3) Play Music; (4) Sing the Party Song; (5) Pay Deepest Respects to the Party, National Flag, and Portrait of the Premier; (6) Reverently Recite the Premier’s Will; (7) Sing the School Song; (8) Chairman's Address; (9) Guest Speeches; (10) President's Address (recorded below); (11) Play Music; (12) Ceremony to Open the Gates; (13) Unveiling Ceremony; (14) Photograph; (15) Adjournment.

School's Congratulatory Message: Our Tongji, founded on medicine and engineering, newly built and magnificent. Talented individuals of the past soared on high paths, with superb skills becoming the nation's glory. Aspiring students, seeing the sea, know the ford. Fine steeds travel thousands of miles, possessing precious jade. Celebrating this anniversary, presenting talents and skills, offering words of blessing, comparable to fine jade.

President's Address: President Hu Shuhua said, "Distinguished guests, colleagues, students, today is the 24th anniversary of our university. We are honored and grateful for the presence of Chinese and foreign guests. Compared to European and American universities with two to four or five hundred years of history, our 24-year-old university is nothing to celebrate. However, among all universities in China, while some were established earlier, perhaps none have experienced such difficulties and repeated destruction as our university. Therefore, the name 'Tongji' (同濟) was chosen to mean 'crossing a river in the same boat during a storm.' Fourteen years ago, we suffered the biggest storm, almost capsizing the entire boat. At that time, not only were our teachers and students oppressed by the French, leading to displacement, but also all our books, instruments, specimens, and buildings were confiscated. If it weren't for the dedication of Mr. Yuan Guanlan and other gentlemen, we wouldn't have today's 24th-anniversary celebration. Without Dr. Bao Long, there would be no medical school at our university. Without Dr. Berentze, there would be no engineering school at our university. Detailed information is available in the special publication and will not be repeated here. To commemorate the achievements of these three gentlemen, alumni have donated funds to erect three memorial steles in the Great Auditorium of Datongji University (a gift from the Tongguang Photography Society).

The unveiling ceremony will take place today. Simultaneously, the dedication ceremony of the newly built Physiological Research Institute will also be held today. Physiology is the most important basic science of the medical school, and construction was planned four or five years ago, but was hindered by a lack of funds. Only today can it be completed. The year before last November, I risked signing the contract for the construction of the Physiological Research Institute, knowing that temporary funding would not be available. We only hoped that the government would issue monthly operating expenses, and we would try our best to save two to three thousand yuan each month for construction costs. Unexpectedly, the war broke out last year, resulting in the non-payment of expenses for October, November, and December of last year, and over five thousand yuan for September to this day. Personally, I have been under pressure from all sides, and the mental anguish is truly indescribable. Fortunately, the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture subsidized 20,000 yuan, which allowed the completion of the water, electricity, gas, and heating equipment of the Physiological Research Institute. More than 70,000 yuan has been spent, but important instruments are still lacking. However, if we hadn't started construction the year before, everything would be more expensive now, and the school's financial resources would be even more difficult to cope with. For this, we must thank the support and efforts of all colleagues. Our university trains specialized talents in applied sciences, which is fully in line with the direction of educational facilities decided by this National Assembly. We hope that the government and society will provide full assistance, and that distinguished guests will provide full guidance, so that our university can continue to develop and prosper. Our graduates serve society with the spirit of scientific patriotism, enhancing the university's reputation. Students in school should study hard with the spirit of saving the country and being unwilling to neglect their studies, raising the university's status. By the time of the 25th-anniversary celebration next year, we will hold a more grand celebration."

After the Establishment of the Military Law Tribunal

The Shanghai Provisional Military Law Tribunal was officially established yesterday. Details were noted in yesterday’s newspaper. The organizational outline and trial rules are recorded as follows:

Organizational Outline: Article 1. The Provisional Military Law Tribunal is organized by personnel sent from the following institutions: (1) Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters; (2) Shanghai Municipal Government; (3) Jiangsu Higher Court; (4) Songhu Garrison Command. The institution mentioned in item (1) of the preceding paragraph may not send personnel to participate in the organization. Article 2. The Provisional Military Law Tribunal has jurisdiction over cases involving communists with serious circumstances or their key offenders. Cases mentioned in the preceding paragraph, after the implementation of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Endangering the Republic of China, within the martial law area or bandit suppression area mentioned in Article 7 of the law, are not under the jurisdiction of the Provisional Military Law Tribunal. Article 3. The judges of the Provisional Military Law Tribunal shall be two personnel sent from the institution mentioned in item (4) of Article 1, and one personnel sent from each of the other institutions. They shall mutually elect one of them as the presiding judge. If the total number of judges sent by the various institutions mentioned in the preceding paragraph is an even number, the Higher Court may send one additional personnel. Article 4. The Provisional Military Law Tribunal shall have several clerks, with one as the chief. The clerks mentioned in the preceding paragraph may be concurrently held by staff members of the institutions listed in Article 1. Scribes may be employed for writing documents. Article 5. The official seal of the Provisional Military Law Tribunal shall be issued by the Songhu Garrison Command. Article 6. The expenses of the Provisional Military Law Tribunal shall be jointly provided by the Songhu Garrison Command and the Shanghai Municipal Government. Article 7. The trial rules of the Provisional Military Law Tribunal shall be separately determined. Article 8. The detailed rules of procedure of the Provisional Military Law Tribunal shall be formulated by the Songhu Garrison Command in conjunction with the Shanghai Municipal Government and submitted to the Executive Yuan and the Judicial Yuan for record. Article 9. This outline shall be implemented from the date of approval by the National Government.

Trial Rules: Article 1. These rules are formulated in accordance with Article 7 of the Organizational Outline of the Provisional Military Law Tribunal of each province. Article 2. The trial of the Provisional Military Law Tribunal shall be conducted by a joint panel of judges. No trial may be opened unless more than half of the judges are present. Article 3. The Provisional Military Law Tribunal does not apply the defense system. Article 4. The trial of the Provisional Military Law Tribunal may not be public. Article 5. For cases accepted by the Provisional Military Law Tribunal, the presiding judge may designate one of the judges to conduct a preliminary investigation of the evidence. After the judge completes the investigation, or if it is deemed that the facts are clear and no investigation is necessary, the presiding judge shall be requested to convene a joint trial. Article 6. If it is deemed that a case accepted by the Provisional Military Law Tribunal is not under its jurisdiction, it shall be immediately transferred to the competent government office. However, if one person commits multiple crimes and one of them is under its jurisdiction, the remaining crimes may be tried together in accordance with the respective articles of law. Article 7. The presiding judge and the judge investigating the evidence may issue summonses to the defendant, witnesses, and informants. Arrest warrants may be issued to the defendant or witnesses, and detention warrants may be issued to the defendant. Search warrants may be issued for searching for evidence. Article 8. The interrogation at the trial shall be conducted by the presiding judge. Judges attending the trial may declare to the presiding judge that they will conduct the interrogation themselves. Article 9. When starting the interrogation, the name, age, native place, address, and occupation shall be inquired first to verify whether there is any error in the person. Article 10. When there are several defendants, they shall be interrogated separately. However, if necessary, other defendants, witnesses, and informants may be ordered to confront each other. Article 11. When interrogating the defendant, the suspicion of his crime shall be inquired in detail one by one. If there is any explanation, he shall be ordered to point out the method of proof. Article 12. When interrogating witnesses or informants, they shall first be informed that they must make truthful statements, and that if there is perjury or false accusation, they shall be punished according to law. After they have made a written oath, they shall be ordered to make their statements. Article 13. The interrogation shall be recorded by the clerk attending the trial, and the statements of the interrogated person shall be clearly recorded. The recording shall be read aloud to the interrogated person in court. If the interrogated person believes that there is an error, the clerk shall record the corrected statement together. If it is deemed that there is no error, the interrogated person shall be ordered to sign or fingerprint it. Article 14. For cases where the presiding judge believes that the interrogation is over, all judges participating in the interrogation shall be convened for deliberation and resolution, and the deliberations shall be signed and sealed. Article 16. The verdict of the joint trial shall be based on the deliberations and resolutions of the preceding article. The clerk shall be ordered to prepare the judgment, which shall be signed and sealed by the presiding judge and all judges participating in the deliberations. It shall be submitted to the Songhu Garrison Command for approval, and it shall be finalized, reported to the Shanghai Municipal Government, and sent to the Shanghai Special City Party Headquarters and the Jiangsu Higher Court for record. Article 17. In cases where several people are co-offenders, even if some have not been brought to justice, a verdict may be made on those who have been brought to justice first. Article 18. If the Songhu Garrison Command believes that there is an error in the judgment, it may be sent back for review. Article 19. After the judgment is finalized, the defendant shall be ordered to appear in court. After the clerk reads the cause of action, the presiding judge shall announce the main text of the judgment. Article 20. The execution of the judgment shall be directed by the presiding judge. When executing the death penalty, the presiding judge shall appoint a supervising officer to be present. Except with the permission of the presiding judge, no one may enter the execution ground. Article 21. These rules shall be implemented from the date of approval by the National Government.

US Restriction on Acidity of Egg Yolk

Opinion of the Commodity Inspection Bureau's Response to the Ministry

Regarding the US restriction of egg yolk acidity to 5 degrees, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, based on a telegram from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, deemed the matter to concern China's international trade and the health of US citizens. Whether the current US method of limiting acidity to 5 degrees is fair, and to what extent the limit should be relaxed so that both parties are not hindered, requires academic research and cannot be argued with empty words. The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau was ordered to conduct thorough research based on scientific methods and report back for verification. After receiving the order, the Bureau instructed Yuan Kaiji, a technician specializing in egg product inspection at the Livestock Product Inspection Division, to conduct a detailed and careful study and submit a preliminary report to the Ministry of Industry. The report stated, "According to the technician, after extensively researching egg product inspection books and past experience in inspecting dried egg yolks and dried whole eggs exported from Shanghai over the past year, the most common acidity is between 2 and 3 degrees, and those exceeding 5 degrees account for about one-sixth of the total exports. If Chinese egg merchants pay a little more attention, they should be able to cope with the US government's acidity limit of 5 degrees. After taking samples and conducting simple experiments, it can be inferred that if fresh and undamaged eggs are used as raw materials and the manufacturing process is very clean, even if egg merchants wait for a price and ship the eggs to the US, even if it takes a long time or they are stored at high temperatures, the acidity should not exceed 5 degrees. If Chinese egg merchants want to maintain their export egg yolk business, they should pay attention to selecting raw materials and improving manufacturing methods to avoid increasing acidity, which would give the US government an excuse." The Bureau also recommended, based on the test results, that the acidity of egg yolks inspected by various inspection bureaus for shipment to the US should be set at 4.5 degrees. Any exceeding this number should not be allowed to be exported to avoid being inspected and denied entry into the US after arrival, causing even greater losses to merchants.

Native Cloth Has Resumed Shipping Yesterday

More than 70 native cloth businesses in Shanghai have requested the tax authorities to exempt native cloth, which is a handmade product, from export duties. The suspension of shipping has lasted for exactly four weeks. Yesterday, cloth merchants went to the Jianghai Customs to declare shipments of native cloth bound for Dongbei (Northeast China), including Harbin, Andong, and Yingkou. There were no more problems. From yesterday onward, cloth merchants officially resumed shipping. According to Li Zuyong, Secretary of the National Revenue Administration of the Ministry of Finance, Director Zhang of the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance sent a message to the Administration on the same day, ordering the Chief Inspectorate of Customs to exempt native cloth shipped from Shanghai merchants to various ports in Dongbei, in areas where the national revenue tax is not yet implemented, and to foreign countries such as Hong Kong and Nanyang, from customs duties and release them for shipment. The Administration was instructed to inform the various customs commissioners to comply. Upon learning that the Shanghai Jianghai Customs had received the order from the Chief Inspectorate of Customs, I went to the Shanghai Customs to meet with both Chinese and foreign Customs Commissioners Ding Guitang and Mei Wushi, urging the Customs to issue a public notice so that native cloth merchants could resume shipping as soon as possible. Cloth merchants have been resuming shipping since yesterday.

Zhejiang's Paper Industry Publishing

Zhejiang Province has been famous for its paper production since ancient times, so it can be said to be an important paper production area in history. Now, with the loss of ancient methods, a lack of desire for improvement, and a shortage of raw materials such as rattan and paper mulberry, there are few who pay attention in society, leading to stagnation and errors. The Zhejiang Provincial Government Design Council, in view of this, engaged in a province-wide paper industry survey. It took one year across 50 counties to complete. All kinds of charts will be compiled and statistically prepared by the Council, with a total of 43 paper-producing counties, 85 types of paper, a total capital of 5,090,028 yuan, an annual output value of 20,850,487 yuan, 24,437 vat households, 27,765 paper vats, and 126,856 workers. Looking at the above, the annual output value of paper in Zhejiang Province is indeed impressive. However, most of this huge sum of more than 20 million yuan is crude paper, only enough for superstitious paper foil qiao paper and packaging paper coarse paper. It is not as good as the output of Fujian, Jiangxi, Anhui and other provinces, although not abundant, but the products are more refined. Therefore, all papers for major uses in art and printing must be imported from foreign countries and Fujian, Jiangxi, Anhui and other provinces. The reasons for the decline are roughly (1) the degradation of papermaking technology, (2) the shortage of capital, and (3) the obstruction of transportation. If this continues, the future of Zhejiang's paper industry will be unimaginable. The materials obtained from this entire survey have long been compiled by the former Design Council and edited into a special publication called "Zhejiang's Paper Industry." It has now been published and details the history and current situation of handmade papermaking, machine papermaking, and Zhejiang paper, the import and export of paper in the country, and the path to the development of the paper industry. There are also prefaces by Mr. Wu Zhihui, Li Shizeng, Zhang Jingjiang, Luo Xitong, 30 papermaking statistical charts, and 23 photographs. The entire book has more than 800 pages and is rich in content. It is a new book that builders, industrialists, and politicians cannot afford to miss. In addition to being distributed by the Construction Committee's Economic Survey of Zhejiang, major bookstores inside and outside the province also sell it.

Fixed Sea Bridge Qining Temple Reduced River Ferry Fare

Originally: 8 Copper Coins per Passenger

Reduced: 4 Copper Coins per Passenger

In order to facilitate transportation on both sides of the Huangpu River, the Municipal Public Works Bureau held a river ferry between the Fixed Sea Bridge on the west bank and the Qining Temple on the east bank. It officially opened on the 16th of this month. The original fare charged per person each time was 8 copper coins. However, most of the ferry passengers were workers, who believed the fare was too high and unaffordable, and requested a reduction. The Bureau believed that the city-run ferry was intended to facilitate the public and was not for profit. Therefore, it immediately obtained the approval of the Municipal Government to temporarily halve the original fare, charging 4 copper coins per passenger each time.

Dong Yu's Wife Sues the Special District Court

Telling the Story of Abuse

Requesting Confirmation of Identity

Paying Appropriate Alimony

Dong Yu's wife, Jiang, submitted a statement to the Shanghai Special District Court, stating that she had been abandoned by her husband and asked the court to confirm her identity and provide alimony. The plaintiff, Jiang, was originally from central Anhui and followed her husband to Jiang Zuo. In the tenth year of the Republic of China, she was introduced by her relative, former Minister of Justice Dong Kang, and betrothed to the defendant, Dong Yu's nephew, Xun Yu. In the winter of that year, the defendant formally married Ms. Lu in Jinan, Shandong. When the plaintiff's family learned of this, they wrote to Dong Kang to inquire. Dong Kang advised Dong Yu to quickly terminate the marriage contract to avoid future disputes. The defendant said that there was no problem with Jiang being the wife and Lu being the concubine. His cousin Dong Banggan provided a letter to prove the plaintiff's identity. In the ninth month of the lunar calendar in the eleventh year, the defendant came to Shanghai to live with the plaintiff's family. Everything was simple, and the necessary wedding expenses were about 300 yuan. All clothes and jewelry were missing. The plaintiff also thought of her simple life and only hoped to maintain a happy family, never mentioning the details. Only ten days after the marriage, the plaintiff scraped together travel expenses and went north with the defendant. For the first three months, they were still loving. Later, because his position as an appointed clerk in the Shandong Higher Court was poorly paid, he asked to live with Ms. Lu. The plaintiff reluctantly agreed to his request. Unexpectedly, after entering the door, Ms. Lu actually managed the household affairs. From then on, the treatment was very different. In the spring of the twelfth year, the plaintiff returned south for childbirth. She told her mother's family everything and asked Dong Kang to convey to the defendant that he should improve her treatment and confirm the status of wife and concubine. The defendant then wrote a paper, guaranteeing everything. In the autumn, the plaintiff gave birth to a daughter and returned north. Before a month had passed, he was dismissed from the court and returned south. The defendant, being unemployed, sent the plaintiff back to her mother's house temporarily. After mediation, he was taken back to live together. After a few months, he abused and expelled her. The plaintiff entrusted Suzhou lawyer Lu Hongyi to send a letter of inquiry, but the defendant ignored it. In recent years, the defendant has been engaged in the practice of law, not so successful. Later, after mediation, the plaintiff was welcomed back in the spring of the eighteenth year and placed in the pavilion room. In addition to giving a few yuan per month (only about 100 yuan in a year), he never provided any clothing. But for Ms. Lu, he bought a car and drove around in social situations every day. The plaintiff's clothes were gorgeous, like a noble woman. In October of last year, Ms. Lu died of measles. The defendant claimed that the plaintiff had poisoned her to death, adding to the animosity. Whenever the plaintiff returned to her mother's house for something, the servant was ordered to close the door and refuse entry. One day, she entrusted a relative to say that the entire rented house would be sold, ordering the plaintiff to find another house, otherwise, she would be expelled as easily as picking up a snail with two fingers. Another day, she went to Dong Kang's place and said that she wanted to divorce the plaintiff. After Dong Kang advised him sternly, he left without success. On November 27, the defendant actually filed a lawsuit in the public court, claiming that the plaintiff had suffered from lung disease before the marriage, requesting a divorce and demanding compensation for wedding expenses of 3,000 yuan. After several hearings, Chief Gong ordered mediation, but the defendant was not sincere. He recruited women to his residence every day, and the family order was unspeakable. In January of this year, Fan Songji volunteered to mediate and said that the defendant had fallen in love with other women, and the divorce must be achieved. He instructed the plaintiff to reluctantly agree to his request, and in the future, when he realized it, he might be able to reunite. Fan Songji stipulated several conditions. On the evening of February 3, Fan Songji invited the plaintiff to a room in the New World Hotel to discuss the matter. The plaintiff thought it was a preliminary consultation and went with Dong Kang's concubine, Ms. Chi. The defendant was also in the next room and had invited lawyer Zhan Jifeng to the scene to prove it, ordering the plaintiff to sign the divorce agreement immediately. The plaintiff believed that the conditions were not appropriate and firmly refused to agree. She stayed until 1:30 in the evening before returning. The next day, the public court opened the trial. The defendant cited the old rules of the public court and advocated an indefinite postponement. Chief Gong ordered a week to resolve the matter in court. The plaintiff was ashamed to be a divorced woman and also filed a request for a verdict. When the deadline was reached, she entrusted lawyer Sheng Shengxi to appear in court, knowing that Chief Gong had agreed to the defendant's request to suspend the case. Recently, the defendant is willing to go to Hong Kong to find a livelihood, claiming that he will sell the residence in Xifei Lane in the French Concession, showing that the plaintiff is willing to return to nothing. The plaintiff heard the news that some clothing and other items had not been taken out, so Dong Banggan went to take them. The defendant happened to be in his law firm and was severely reprimanded by the servant's phone call, claiming that whoever took one item would be sent to the court as a robber for investigation. The plaintiff, terrified by his power, stopped immediately. The defendant rushed home and informed the French police, willing to arrest the plaintiff. By the time the plaintiff had left. This is the true situation of the plaintiff's marriage by fraud and the brutal treatment and recent abandonment by the defendant. I have been self-conscious of the fact that the plaintiff was born in a famous family,拘于礼教, 贻误至今 (I can't translate this well, and I'm not adding comments). If the defendant regarded Ms. Lu as the first wife, when the plaintiff declared the termination of the marriage contract, he should not have used fraudulent means to conclude this invalid marriage. He confirmed the plaintiff's identity, and he should not have dismissed the repeated letters and declared Ms. Lu as the first wife. Within the statute of limitations for criminal liability, the relatives of both parties repeatedly advised him to file a criminal lawsuit. The plaintiff, believing in the righteousness of a single marriage, could not bear to put the defendant in prison. Last year, this newspaper specially dispatched photography reporters Wang Xiaoting and Liu Shuofu to accompany Mr. Smith of the Chicago Museum of Natural History in the United States on a biological collection trip to Sichuan. After leaving Shanghai in November, they passed through Chongqing, Xufu, Jiading, and Yazhou, and photographed many scenery scenes in Sichuan along the way, and a small part has been published in this newspaper's pictorial. Later, Wang and Liu, because the collection group's scope was not wide, immediately set off separately, traveling to the Qiangyi-Tibetan tribes on the northwestern border of Sichuan, passing through Dajinchuan, Xiaojinchuan, Hou Chuan, Weizhou, Lifean, Zagu Brain, Daweijia, Jinshan, Maogong, Yutong, Muping, and other places in Dajianlu. They took many unique photos of various high-altitude snow scenes, Tibetan Yi village houses, customs, and clothing, and collected valuable and interesting textual materials from each place. There are true situations that are different from the records of various families. At the same time, after the problem of the Kangzang dispute broke out, the real situation inside was far from what was reported outside, and many photos of our army and the Tibetan army fighting were taken, which are extremely valuable for proving the Kangzang incident. Recently, this newspaper received letters from the two gentlemen, saying that they will meet in Jiading soon and then return east, and they are expected to arrive in Shanghai at the end of the month. Mr. Wang also went to Mount Gongga (the second highest peak in the world, about 26,000 feet above sea level, to take pictures, which is also rare outside. In the future, it will be published successively in this newspaper's pictorial, and texts will be published in this newspaper.

A Girl's Head Cut Off By Streetcar

The Girl Xu Da-Nian Died A Pitiable Death

Yesterday's report described a girl riding in a trolley car, traveling near the vegetable market on Avenue Edward VII, when she leaned her head out of the window and struck an electric pole along the road, causing her head to break and bleed, resulting in death. It is now known that the deceased was named Xu Da-Nian and was only ten years old. She was the daughter of Xu Yufang of Zhenjiang. The trolley car she was riding was number 349 on Route 16. Her body was ordered to be carried into the Filun Road Examination Office by the Xinzha Police Station. Yesterday morning, all the witnesses were summoned to the office. At 10:00 AM, the Special District Court Prosecutor's Office appointed Prosecutor Guo Huaipu to come to the office to investigate. He ascended to the seat of public office and questioned the driver of the car, Li Xueren, who said that because the place where the accident occurred was under construction, the trolley car was driving along the side of the road and moving very slowly. Unexpectedly, the girl suddenly leaned her head out of the window, causing the disaster. Mr. Miller, a Westerner from the trolley car company, also submitted a statement, saying that all trolley cars have rules posted inside warning passengers not to lean their heads out of the window while the trolley car is moving, which is also stated in the rules. Although women and children may not know everything, fathers and elder brothers should also explain it in detail on weekdays so that such a tragedy does not happen. Finally, the father of the deceased requested that the company be ordered to provide compensation for the funeral. Prosecutor Guo then instructed the Westerner to return to the company to negotiate and provide some compensation, and instructed Xu Yufang to collect the body for burial.

Li Zongkan's Case: Kidnappers Sentenced to Five Years

Li Zongkan, the nephew of Li Shizeng, a member of the Central Committee residing at No. 584 Father Laro, French Concession, was an engineer at the Dafang Construction Company. A few days ago, he went out from home and took his own car to go to the company to work. Unexpectedly, as soon as he got into the car, six kidnappers rushed up, trying to kidnap him. Fortunately, Li opened the car door and escaped. Special detectives and supervisors from the French Police Department, including Jin Jiulin, chief detective Li Yaolong, deputy detectives Qian Yumin and Zhang Ziying, and Mao Jingen, heard the alarm and rushed to the scene, capturing one kidnapper, Wang Afu, and finding a handgun on his person, and taking him to the police station for investigation. The police sent Wang to the French court for investigation. The plaintiff first complained about the kidnapping. When asked, Wang Afu confessed that he was from Tongzhou and had been a vendor. He was invited by Lu Haitao, whom he had known for a long time, to kidnap the plaintiff, which was true. He also hired a lawyer to represent him in everything. The Chinese and Western officials sentenced Wang Afu to five years in Western prison and deportation, and sent him to the inland court for investigation. The handgun was confiscated.

Ye Chen's Case Has Hope for Mediation

Rescheduled for Retrial in Two Weeks

The case of Ye Zhongfang being accused by Chen Yan, the wife of the late lawyer Chen Zhigang, of seducing her daughter Chen Xiuzhen, was continued by the Special District Court, because the police at the Lukiawan Police Station in the French Concession had to investigate the plaintiff's report of her daughter's abduction in the past, so the case was postponed. Yesterday afternoon, the date of the continued hearing was reached, and both parties filed the case on time, but the Lukiawan Police Station had not yet replied with a clear document to the court and could not proceed with the trial. The defendant's lawyer said that mediation has made progress and requested a rescheduling of two weeks to continue the mediation outside the court. At that time, the plaintiff's side did not object, so Judge Xiao Xieffun approved the defendant's request and ordered a retrial in two weeks.

Male Corpse Found Floating in Zhoujiadu

A male corpse, about thirty years old, wearing blue cloth short clothes, resembling a drowned person, was found floating in the Nanxiao River in Zhoujiadu, Pudong, yesterday morning. Because there were no family members, the local security guard of the 10th and 11th districts reported to the local court for examination.

Car Kills Person

Driver Tries to Flee After Causing Accident

Tao Weibiao, a Cantonese accountant from a Cantonese restaurant in Hongkou, was sixty-three years old this year. On the 19th of this month, he went to the south of the city for business and returned north at 11:50 PM. When he was traveling through the intersection of Avenue Edward VII and Zilai Street, a car No. 2910 driven by driver Chen Afu (the car belongs to the owner of the Qu Changshun Fish Shop at No. 47 Xiaodongmen Street) drove from west to east on Avenue Edward VII at high speed, causing Tao to not be able to avoid it in time and was knocked to the ground, injuring his head. The police saw him and recorded the number, but the driver fled out of fear. The police caught him and took him to the police station. The injured person was sent to Renji Hospital, but died at 7:00 AM yesterday morning due to his injuries. The hospital notified the police to take the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Office for examination. At that time, because there were no family members, the French Police Vehicle Office reported to Judge Zhu Chengshen of the French Public Concession, who came to the office at noon to examine the body. The Vehicle Office brought the defendant driver to the case. After questioning by Mr. Zhu, he ordered the body to be photographed and collected by the hall, waiting for the family to claim it. The defendant was released on bail pending verification. After the examination, the family members arrived at the autopsy office to identify him and reported to the Vehicle Office to collect the body. The family members have now hired lawyer Yan Dajue to file a lawsuit.

Pedestrian Severely Injured By Car

At about 1:30 yesterday morning, a pedestrian, about fifty years old, wearing an old cloth cotton robe, was traveling through Zilai Street on Avenue Edward VII when he was suddenly knocked to the ground by a car number 17875, causing severe head injuries. He was taken by police officer No. 573 from the Grand Autophone Police Station and taken to Renji Hospital for treatment. It is said that the injury was too severe, and there may be danger to his life.

Counter-Revolutionary Elements of China Public School Transferred to Court

The Shanghai Executive Committee learned that students Zhang Guohui, Wan Shizuo, Hou Shuzhang, Li Jingxi, Zhao Xuanting, Luo Guangfu, Kang Yu, etc. of Wusong China Public School are well-known counter-revolutionaries, who have conspiracies to endanger the Party and subvert the government, and have exposed the destruction of the Prime Minister's portrait and the national flag in the school's auditorium. The district party headquarters was instructed to cooperate with the police station in the seventh district to send police to arrest them. Except for Zhang Guohui, who escaped, the rest were arrested and sent to the Public Security Bureau. When questioned, all the defendants denied it. The Public Security Bureau immediately sent a letter to inquire about the party headquarters, and learned that the fugitive Zhang Guohui was the leader of the Communist Party, Wan Shizuo was the leader of the National Socialist Party, and the rest were involved in counter-revolution. Since the Public Security Bureau had been identified by the party headquarters, it transferred them to the local court for investigation yesterday.

Sheng Huang First Day on Stage A Great Success

Famous actor Xun Huisheng, was hired by the Grand Theater to perform in Shanghai. In recent days, various circles have held banquets to welcome him and presented gifts. Last night was the first day to perform. Before 8:00, it was full. The walls on both sides of the stage and along the flower building were full of paintings, calligraphy, silk embroidery, etc., either horizontal plaques, vertical scrolls, couplets, or mirror screens. Silver tripods, silver shields, silver cups, silver screens, flower baskets, etc. were lined up in front of the stage, dazzling and beautiful. Due to the limited location, more than forty pieces of screens, couplets, etc. that were temporarily received could not be hung. When Xun Guan Niang came on stage, the applause and cheers from the audience were like spring thunder. Xun's demeanor was even more beautiful than last year, and his singing skills also improved. Xun Guan Niang is his masterpiece, and every move and every tune was praised by the audience. Looking back on Xun's visit to Shanghai, it has been seven times. The enthusiastic welcome of the audience was the most grand last night. Tonight, he will perform Xiangluo Belt, and tomorrow night, he will perform Qipan Mountain, both of which are Xun's self-compiled masterpieces. Although Qipan Mountain is an old drama, no one has performed it in Shanghai or Tianjin. It is expected that the audience will be more enthusiastic than the first night.

The "Kinema Record" Published Today

The monthly magazine "Kinema Record," edited by Mr. Zhou Shixun, since its publication, has been deeply welcomed by readers because it does not publish advertisements from film companies and its arguments are loyal and its writing interesting. In recent months, its sales have been very broad. The recently published eighth issue is a special issue on physical culture, and its content is even more exquisite. In addition to twelve finely printed new photos of health stars, it also publishes more than a hundred health star illustrations, as well as specially featured famous works, many health and beauty maxims, and a health star mailing list. Readers with this book in hand can write to science stars for small photos. The magazine is published by Wenhua Bookstore. Innovation at the Meiwen Printing House

The Meiwen Printing House, located east of the Risheng Building on Nanjing Road, was founded by Mr. Zhang Ziliang. It has been in operation for many years. Its equipment for printing is very complete. In addition to printing colorful lithographs, letterpress prints, and all kinds of large and small printed materials, it has recently established a Western-language printing department to provide customers with translation, typesetting, and printing services. In addition, it also has various sizes of imitation Song typeface, which other printing companies cannot match. It is said that if there is an urgent need for printed materials, and the customer wants to pick them up within a limited number of days, overtime work can be added day and night to rush the printing.

The inclusion of reward offers further increases the reader's interest. The annual subscription is only one yuan and fifty cents in silver.

Nationally Invented Sound Film Camera

Mr. Yan Hemen, a photographer at the Star Film Company, and Mr. Su Zuguo, a management engineer at the Asia-America Broadcasting Station, have been researching photography and electrical technology for a long time. They have recently invented a sound film camera that records sound on the film. After hundreds of improvements, it has been completed and named "Yan Su Tong," with the English name "Yensutone." During the research period, Mr. Yan and Mr. Su worked up to twenty hours a day for more than a hundred days, using more than ten thousand feet of film. The cost of repeatedly reforming other machines was even greater. It is also reported that all the machines were manufactured by the Asia-America Company's factory. Recently, they have been filming, and it is expected to be released soon.

Far East Aviation Company Actively Expanding

The aircraft sold by the Far East Aviation Company in this port are all products of the British Royal Aviation Company. They are of solid quality and particularly resistant to navigation, and are recognized as the best in military aircraft. The company has strong capital and is actively expanding its business. Previously, it shipped seven military aircraft and Avro trainer aircraft from England to China for demonstration and sample use. Three of them are in Nanjing, one in Liaoning, and three in Hong Kong. Other aviation companies have never had so many aircraft in China for demonstration purposes. This shows the company's strong capital and broad scope.

Pathé Will Release Four-and-a-Half-Minute Records

The Pathé Company on Sichuan Road has been established in China for more than twenty years. Recently, it hired technicians with rich technical experience and is determined to conduct research. It has invented a kind of steel needle record. The area of ​​this record is larger than ordinary steel records, with a diameter of twelve inches, and can play for four and a half minutes, which is one and a half minutes longer than ordinary records that only play for three minutes. The company has now recorded many famous operas by the king of the opera world, Mei Lanfang, and the leading figure of the old male role, Ma Lianliang, either duets or solos. Not only is there no sand noise, but it is also clear and loud, with extremely satisfactory results. It is said that it will be released soon, and then the music lovers can once again enjoy a feast for their ears.

The "New Taicang Daily" is the only publication of the youth community in Taicang County in Shanghai. Its purpose is pure and its arguments are fair. It has always been respected by society. It was discontinued for more than two years due to lack of leadership. Now, the former employees of the newspaper who are in Shanghai are becoming increasingly numerous. Letter

Sir, According to the person concerned, Mr. Bao Fangzhou, yesterday (19th) your newspaper published an article about the Fangzhou case, which had errors in the facts concerning me and the names of others. I am commissioned to write to your newspaper and ask for corrections, etc. I hereby forward the letter and request that you correct the following facts in accordance with the following facts. I am, with respect, the chief writer of Shenbao, Lawyer Yan Dajue, May 20th.

(1) Mr. Bao Fangzhou studied in Japan from a young age. In the first year of the Republic of China, he founded the Chinese Spiritual Research Association in Kobe, Japan. He returned to China in the sixth year of the Republic of China to lecture. At that time, he once gave a performance of [blank space] in the Shanghai Press Club (as evidenced by various newspapers), and then established the Shanghai branch. He has been stationed in Shanghai since the seventh year of the Republic of China.

(2) There are no names of Ms. Liu Chunyi and Mr. Zhang Xueming among the members of the Chinese Spiritual Research Association. There are only the names of Mr. Liu Jifei, Chairman of Chahar Province, and Mr. Zhang Xuezeng, the younger brother of Zhang, the Deputy Commander of Liaoning.

Special Item

Business Report of the Bank of China for the 19th Year of the Republic of China (Continued)

(International Trade in the 19th Year of the Republic of China)

International trade in the 19th year of the Republic of China suffered declines in silver prices, frequent internal wars, harassment by bandits and communists, and a sluggish world market. Although there was no major change in value, the quantity inevitably decreased sharply. According to the customs, the total import and export volume for the year was 2,204,599,336 customs taels (excluding gold and silver). Compared with the total import and export volume of 2,281,466,039 taels in the 18th year, it decreased by 76,866,703 taels, or 3.3 percent. However, compared with the 17th year, there was still an increase of about 17 million taels. The net import value for the year was 1,309,755,742 taels, an increase of 43,976,921 taels over the net import value in the 18th year, or 3.4 percent. The net export value was 894,843,594 taels, a decrease of 220,843,624 taels compared to the net export value in the 18th year, or 11.9 percent. The excess of imports over exports increased from 250,091,603 taels in the 18th year to 414,912,148 taels, a huge number unprecedented. What is even more noteworthy is that although the total import and export volume in the 19th year was only slightly lower than that in the 18th year, this is only in terms of the silver value. If calculated in terms of gold prices, the difference is quite large. The average conversion rate of the customs tael in the 18th year was 2 shillings 7 and 13/16 pence, so the imported goods that year were worth £167,781,617 in British gold. The average conversion rate of the customs tael in the 19th year was 1 shilling 10 and 11/16 pence, so the imported goods that year were only worth £123,810,119 in British gold, a decrease of £43,971,498, or 26 percent. This is the decrease in quantity, which is still slightly better than the 30 percent decrease in imports from Japan. As for the import and export status of various commercial ports, the customs offices in Dalian, Andong, Tianjin, Yantai, Hankou, Guangdong, and Kowloon all saw declines in the 19th year. Shanghai, Shantou, Qingdao, and Harbin all increased. Shanghai alone accounted for 51 percent of import trade and 35 percent of export trade. Dalian ranked second, accounting for 14.4 percent of the total trade. Tianjin ranked third, accounting for 8.2 percent of the total trade. Below this are Guangdong, Qingdao, Harbin, Andong, Shantou, Hankou, and Kowloon in that order. Among the importing countries, Japan ranked first, followed by the United States. India jumped to third place due to the increase in cotton imports. The United Kingdom dropped from third to fourth place. Germany's import volume still cannot compete with Japan, the United States, and the United Kingdom, but it increased by 2 million customs taels compared to the 18th year and nearly doubled compared to before the European War. The country of origin of imports and the value of imported goods are shown below: Importing Country Value of Imported Goods (Customs Taels) Percentage

Among the imported goods, those that decreased were cotton textiles, from 174,126,776 customs taels in the 18th year to 149,888,808 taels in the 19th year, wool textiles from 44,723,417 taels to 24,804,424 taels, and sugar from 98,765,446 taels to 86,390,806 taels. Those that increased were cotton, from 91,123,857 taels to 132,265,669 taels, machinery from 29,886,503 taels to 44,288,207 taels, and chemicals from 34,254,517 taels to 46,904,944 taels. As for food, wheat imports in the 19th year were 2,762,240 dan, a decrease of 2,901,617 dan compared to the 5,663,857 dan in the previous year. Flour imports were 5,188,243 dan, a decrease of 6,747,205 dan compared to the 11,935,448 dan in the previous year. However, rice imports increased to 19,892,784 dan, an increase of 9,068,719 dan compared to the 10,824,066 dan in the previous year. In total, the total value of food imports was approximately 189,262,340 taels, equivalent to approximately 283,893,510 silver dollars, an increase of 21,803,830 taels, equivalent to 32,705,745 silver dollars, compared to the total value of food imports in the previous year of 167,410 taels, equivalent to 251,187,760 silver dollars. China, a country based on agriculture, imports so much food, which is a matter of life and death for the Chinese people. The report for the 18th year already emphasized this three times, but the 19th year has only increased, which is truly a cause for long sighs. The export trade in the 19th year was greatly reduced due to the impact of the sluggish world market, decreasing from 1,015,687,318 customs taels in the 18th year to 894,843,594 taels. The main goods with reduced sales were raw silk, soybeans, tung oil, tea, cotton, leather, feathers, and wool. The export of peanuts and peanut oil increased dramatically. Eggs and egg products were also able to maintain their original state. The country of origin of exports and the value of exported goods are shown below:

Free Talk

World Tidbits

—Hai Ke

The famous Princeton University in the United States conducted zoological experiments. They removed a heart from a turtle and used scientific methods to keep it beating for up to thirty-six hours.

Sea dogs have very poor eyesight out of the water and can barely see anything. Therefore, European and American sea dog skin traders often wait for them to come ashore to play before capturing them in one fell swoop.

There are a total of 50,771 registered blind people in the United Kingdom, of whom 36,485 are unemployed. It can be seen that it is extremely difficult for blind people to find employment.

An American beauty expert says that if women can smile often, it can make their faces look delicate and young. If they constantly give cold faces to others, the lower jaw is prone to overlapping (i.e., what is commonly called a double chin).

The clock face on the Royal Liver Building in Liverpool, England, is thirty feet in diameter. It is the largest clock face of all clocks in the country.

Deauville in France is a famous tourist area. All sounds in the streets are prohibited, especially drums, flutes, dog barks, and car horns are strictly forbidden.

Gleanings from the National Conference

—Jie Fei

The National Conference was held on May 5th amidst drizzle and was closed on May 17th under the blue sky and white sun. As Mr. Hu Shuhua said, "The National Conference is about to rain. This is the spirit of the Premier in heaven, instructing us to share the same boat in this stormy situation… Finally, I remember a German saying: 'After the rain, there will be clear weather.' It usually encourages people to strive for a bright and righteous path from hardship. I believe that all the storms after the National Conference have passed, and we will get a truly blue sky and white sun. I would like to use this meaning to wish the National Conference success." From the opening to the closing, a total of thirteen days passed. Since I was nearby, I had the opportunity to admire it from time to time. Now I record its trivial details to fill this talk.

The Capital on This Day: Since the opening of the National Conference, the streets of the capital have been completely renewed. South of Chengxian Street, memorial archways can be seen along the road. In the evening, colorful electric lights are lit up. The people of the capital are wearing their spring clothes for the first time, giving a sense of everyone being out on the streets. At the same time, all newspapers increased the printing of special issues of the National Conference. The Capital Grand Theatre specially screened "The National Soul" on the opening day, and each time it was sold out. This is enough to prove a glimpse of the excitement and joy of the people of the capital on this day.

Grand Exhibition: Various domestic exhibitions were held in the capital before and after the opening of the National Conference, such as the Jiangsu Special Products Exhibition, the Revolutionary History Exhibition, the Health Exhibition, the Central University Seventeenth Grade Art Exhibition, the Beijing Municipal Art Exhibition, and the Hangzhou Art College Exhibition. They sprung up like bamboo shoots after rain. The people of the capital have been fortunate to feast their eyes in recent days.

Auto Assembly: On the days of the opening and closing ceremonies, cars gathered like ants. Even the spacious plaza of Central University was almost useless. Every day when the meeting was held, cars went in and out at 8:00 AM and 12:00 PM. Cars ran tail to tail on Chengxian Street, sometimes for an hour without stopping. At first, when requesting a car number at the meeting place, the police would shout the number through a megaphone, but it took a long time. Later, because the scope was too wide and the sound did not reach, areas were designated. Representatives lived in certain dormitory numbers, and cars were parked in the area of ​​those numbers. This measure greatly benefited the police.

Plane Tree Spring Sorrow: When expanding the Dazhong Road of Central University, the French plane trees planted on both sides for the past five or six years had trunks as thick as a person's waist and roots more than ten feet long. Cranes were used to move them outward. It took dozens of people an hour to complete the work for each tree. It is said that the transplantation cost for each tree was four yuan and fifty cents.

Evening Scene of the Venue: From Chengxian Street to the venue, there are three pine and cypress memorial archways, all of which are tall and solemn, especially the memorial archway in front of the main gate. It is in the form of an ancient building with three holes underneath. It is more than ten feet high, with flying eaves overlapping each other, capturing the beauty of ancient Chinese architecture, and its meaning is very profound. Every time the lights are lit, the electric lights compete to shine, and many tourists look from afar. The Great Auditorium is especially brilliant in the evening. Thousands of lights are connected together, illuminating the distant forest and flowers. There is a view of spring light like the sea. Its magnificent and towering, occasionally walking under the pillars, makes one feel like a wriggling insect. The thought of reverence is often heartfelt.

Mr. Fan Shutong Came to Shanghai from Shashi to Visit Old Friends, and Upon Reading the Great Collection, Inscribed Two Quatrains to Present

—Cheng Yansheng

His style is as straightforward as Chen Wuyi, and his life is somewhat similar to Yuan Yuzhi. His bitter words and long chants are due to his ultimate nature, and he lies exhausted in Shashi, fearing to be known.

His lofty footprints come from far away, the Yangtze and Han rivers last forever. In the fading spring, wind and rain fall upon the flowers. There are few remaining loyal subjects on the sea, and the sick and old man can be visited. (Referring to the two gentlemen, Wang Bingshan and Zhu Qiangcun)

Accompanying the Two Dukes, Ren and Wen, to Visit the Wu Zhuang Shrine in Gyeongseong, Korea

—Pan Yang'an

The general's great achievements are inscribed in the green history, leaving behind the incense of sacrifice in the three Hans. Ten thousand cherry blossoms bloom near the three-foot tablet. I gaze upon the general's temple and my clothes are stained with tears.

His demeanor is no different from Yang Shuzi, and his meritorious name does not yield to Li Rusong. Who can take on the role of the mainstay in the middle of the stream today? The difficulties of the country make me miss the general even more.

Visiting the Royal Palace in Gyeongseong, Korea

—Pan Yang'an

I cannot bear to recall the events of the Tianbao era. The white-haired old men speak of the vicissitudes of life. The ancient palace and secret garden are still unharmed today. The high Northern Han Mountain leans against the setting sun.

Another Dream

— Tao Zaidong

I was a callow youth, following my late father in exile to the Xueping area within Xiangtan County city in Hunan. Xueping was an open space in front of the school palace, directly abutting the southern city wall. Its gate was named Guānxiāng. Xiangtan's commerce was historically prosperous; the streets and markets were collectively known as "Zǒng." Outside Guānxiāng Gate was the Jiǔ Zǒng, extending upstream to the Shíbā Zǒng, a length of perhaps twenty miles, with the Shíwǔ and Liù Zǒng areas especially known as a gathering place for elites. On the night of the twelfth day of the seventh month in the Gēngyín year of the Guangxu reign, I had a dream. I dreamt that the Shíwǔ and Liù Zǒng area was careless, with red light reaching the sky. From afar, I heard the clamor of voices, interspersed with a sound like a string of firecrackers. Waking, I remembered it. Local Xiangtan custom forbade speaking of dreams in the morning. After breakfast, I related it. My late father said, "You must have dreamt what you were thinking. At the time, it was the Zhongyuan Festival. Xiangtan customs involved ancestral sacrifices, with households burning paper money, all in Xueping. Dozens or hundreds of such events occur daily, their light blazing. You probably had a dream based on these impressions." This theory seemed highly plausible. Two days later, on the fourteenth, at dusk, I heard alarm gongs clang loudly outside the city. Quickly, I rushed into the city. Soon, water dragons (fire engines) sped past. Civil and military officials and their retinues followed, shouting. After supper, my late father led my brothers and I up to the Guānxiāng Gate tower to observe. As I ascended the city wall and gazed out, I immediately recalled my dream. The fire was indeed raging in the Shíwǔ and Liù Zǒng area. The red light reaching the sky, the clamor of voices mixed with the sound of firecrackers – all matched the dream scene exactly. The sound of firecrackers, I later learned, came from the bamboo shops on River Street, where bamboo poles were made. My late father was also astonished by the strange dream, saying that if I hadn't predicted it beforehand, people would have suspected I was talking nonsense. Dreams are easily forgotten. This dream, because of this incident, remained vividly in my memory. I often asked people about it, but none could explain it. After the founding of the Republic, I served in the Zhejiang Governor's Secretariat, and I told my colleague Ding Guiqiao about it. Guiqiao, a devout Buddhist, showed me the *Notes from the Pingdeng Pavilion* by Di Chuqing. In one entry, the owner kept a goose, and dreamt that the goose was killed by a dog. The next day, the dog indeed killed the goose. The main explanation was that all future events are stored in a person's eighth consciousness field, occasionally appearing in dreams. I am a dull and ignorant person and do not understand this at all. Furthermore, the goose and the dog were both domestic animals, connected to the owner. I, however, am like drifting duckweed, having no connection to Xiangtan at all. That county is a large one, with a population of no less than a million, yet the premonition appeared to a young man with absolutely no connection to it. Why is this? According to the Buddhist teachings of Ding and Di, everything in the world, small as a goose's death or large as a fire, is predetermined. Is there, then, a predetermined fate for even the smallest things? Speaking of myself, I have strived for fame and fortune for decades. Many future good and bad fortunes should be stored in my eighth consciousness. Why is it that I never see them in my dreams, but instead dream of a fire with which I have no connection? I sincerely hope that Ding and Di can offer me an explanation, and that philosophers and spiritualists can enlighten me.

Brief News. The Paris Grand Theater, starting this Thursday, will screen a major social warning film titled "Stealing Jade and Savoring Fragrance." Not only are the plot and performances excellent, but its message is especially pertinent to modern society, provoking deep thought. Modern young men and women often conflate spiritual love with sexual desire, leading to various tragedies. The protagonist of this film also fails to recognize this, resulting in the woman becoming secretly pregnant. Rumors fly, and gossip abounds. The woman's father hears of it and repeatedly seeks to kill her. Fortunately, the man's love is as firm as iron, and they eventually become a couple. However, the woman is already worn down and haggard. There is also an interlude that serves as a warning. At the time, there is another cohabiting man, a master of "stealing jade and savoring fragrance," who has always coveted the woman. When the woman's secret is revealed, many suspect him to be the culprit. The rumor spreads to his lover, who, overwhelmed with grief and anger, jumps out of a window and commits suicide. What thoughts will the gossipy tongues of the world have after watching this? (Sheng Pu)

News from the Publishing World. This book was initially a secret record for students of Zhou's Ningxiang Study in Mo Li. Later, his descendants carefully researched it and revised it into its present form. All the erroneous characters used throughout history are listed in the book, with detailed research, classified annotations, and contained within one hundred rhymes. The text is concise and the meaning comprehensive. The book is printed on Chinese Lian Shi paper in a deluxe hardback volume, priced at only eighty cents of a dollar. Published by the Butterfly Society at No. 5 Sanshan Street, Suzhou. A consignment sales point has also been set up at Peisheng Pharmaceutical Company, No. 203 Zhonghua Road, Nanshi in this city to facilitate purchase by various circles in Shanghai.

Travelogue of the Yellow Sea (9)

— Huang Yanpei

On the morning of April 2nd, I traveled to Korea and arrived in Seoul in the evening.

This is my third trip to Korea. I have many Korean and Japanese friends. Three years ago, I wrote a book titled "Korea." The authorities, knowing that I pay attention to Korean affairs, had the Foreign Affairs Section of the Governor-General's Office guide me to observe educational and cultural institutions and hosted a banquet for me at the Myeongwol Gak. Amid the singing and dancing, a great deal of sorrow naturally arose.

Inscription at Myeongwol Gak

Seoul in the third month, like a spring bath.

The stories from this pavilion still warrant tears.

A telephone then betrayed the names of heroes.

Tonight, beautiful women wear Five Clouds robes.

You rise to dance.

I compose a song.

The song complete, the moonlight is white across the sky,

Illuminating the coming and going waves of the Han River. (In 1919, during the Korean Independence Declaration, patriots gathered at Myeongwol Gak. When the police arrived, they reported their names to the police station by telephone and were all arrested.)

A courtesan named Coral Bead insisted that I write a poem, so I wrote a quatrain:

Red are the coral, white are the pearls.

What is the feeling between beautiful women facing each other?

If we were to meet a bewhiskered stranger from overseas,

He would recognize that heroes are not alone.

Since 1919, Japan's policy toward Korea has been to abolish all unequal treatment between Japan and Korea, and this policy is still being implemented. This is the effect of the two bombs that year. However, equality between Japan and Korea is limited to the surface. In essence, they implement two major policies: (1) Immigration. As mentioned earlier, two million Koreans are moved into South Manchuria to be pioneers in acquiring commercial lease rights. (2) Assimilation. They vigorously promote marriage between Japanese and Koreans. The government awards each such couple one hundred gold coins. However, out of the entire Korean population of nineteen million, there are only four hundred and fifty such couples. I asked Koreans if they would like to marry Japanese. The answer was: "Which man wants a Japanese woman? Which woman is willing to marry a Japanese man?"

Japan is extremely intent on appeasing the Korean people and provoking them to hate our people. Their devious intentions were laid bare long ago in the chapter on Korean immigration incentives and protection policies in the Tanaka Memorial. It states, "If the number of Koreans in Manchuria and Mongolia exceeds 2.5 million, then in the event of an incident, we can use the Korean people as atoms for military activities. However, our country can utilize the Koreans, but we must guard against the Chinese government utilizing the Koreans to control us." For this reason, they are doing their best to alienate Korean feelings toward us.

Rotary Club Stories

The Twists and Turns of the Hawthorne Detective Case (20)

— Cheng Xiaoqing

That afternoon, I did not participate in what Hawthorne said he had to do. He only said that there were several leads that needed to be pursued urgently. However, because my Peiqin was not yet fully recovered, he did not let me go with him, only telling me to go home and wait for news. By the evening of that day, Hawthorne made a phone call, telling me that he was seventy or eighty percent certain about the whereabouts of that young man, and he expected to find out completely soon. I thought to myself that seventy or eighty percent certainty was not far from the complete result, and it could not be considered unwelcome news. As for how Hawthorne achieved seventy or eighty percent certainty, I had no other thoughts besides surprise and admiration. I patiently waited another day. By three or four o'clock the next afternoon, Hawthorne suddenly came to my residence in person. He claimed to be visiting Peiqin's illness. In fact, he brought three pieces of delightful news to me. However, he did not announce this news immediately. It was not until he bid me farewell and I sent him outside the door that he quietly told me. He whispered, "Your experience that night, I assume you concealed it from your wife." I nodded. Hawthorne smiled and said, "Fortunately, I knew better than to reveal it to her face." I said, "But haven't you completely found out the traces of this person?" Hawthorne seemed to imitate my actions, nodding in the same way. I quickly asked, "Who is this person? What kind of character is he?" Hawthorne said, "This person has a big background. His surname is Che and his given name is Shijie. He lives at No. 718 Datong Road. He used to work in the military, so he knew Gao Peixian. Now he is working as a clerk for Lawyer Wen. That Lawyer Wen is still his uncle." I said, "It can't be said to be such a big deal for this person to be a lawyer's clerk." Hawthorne said, "Lawyer Wen's given name is Zhang. Have you heard of him?" Only then did I know that this person specializes in handling cases of adultery and theft, and has some "wicked reputation" in society. He is definitely not a good person to provoke. Before I could answer, Hawthorne continued, "This person makes a living from the law. Since this matter has taken a turn, and he is using indirect means to trick us without leaving any traces, there is really no legal action that can be taken against him. Therefore, we must also think of a roundabout way to retaliate." I hurriedly asked again, "So, how to do it in a roundabout way? Do you already have a plan in mind?" Hawthorne shook his head and said, "Not yet. This can only patiently wait for an opportunity. Acting rashly will only ruin things."

Weak in the Morning, Flourishing in the Afternoon, Up Three Taels and More. Food – Ke Xian Rice Sales Active, Price Increases Slightly

Yesterday, the Ke Xian rice market situation was still very good due to competition among local merchants, and prices jumped slightly. This is because current inventories are low. Once local merchants compete, cargo owners tend to hoard, and if local appetites remain strong in the future, the situation of inventory depletion will worsen, and prices will continue to improve. Yesterday, the overall market opened with 1,500 bags of Jiangxi machine-milled late rice, priced at 11.40 to 11.10 yuan, slightly higher than the previous day. In addition, 300 bags of newly arrived Wuhu machine-milled Xian rice were priced at 10.08 to 10.03 yuan. Other goods were scarce and did not open for trading.

1,500 Tons Newly Traded

Moreover, the high price of gold has made the combined price more expensive. Forward Wheat Fluctuates Several Times

Resulting in Only a Slight Decrease

Yesterday, the forward wheat market opened in the morning, and prices for all months showed an upward trend again. With the quoted price of foreign wheat returning to a high of 2 to 3 cent, and the weather still cloudy and rainy, the surrounding environment became increasingly unfavorable. Therefore, after the opening price, due to the enthusiasm of the people, the market jumped violently again. This month's price reached a high of 4.30 taels, June reached 2.5 cent, July reached 2.2 cent, August reached 2.3 cent, and October reached 2.8 cent, a sharp increase of 4, 5, 6, or 7 cent compared to the previous day's closing price. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, with the weather clearing up, and the rumor spreading that factories had ordered 30,000 tons of foreign wheat, and foreign merchants' sales efforts remained active, people's hearts had already become weak. The general expectation was that prices would fall, so selling increased, and the market plummeted. However, compared to the previous day's closing price, the drop was not much. As a result, this month decreased slightly by 7 cent, June and July decreased slightly by 2 cent, August and September decreased slightly by 1 cent, and October decreased slightly by 3 cent, it is said.

Flour Market Advances and Retreats Quickly

The Final Decrease Was Slight

Yesterday, the flour market opened in the morning, and prices for all months remained lively. With the weather cloudy and rainy, and the quoted price of foreign wheat higher, speculators were very active. May, June, and July all broke through the 1 cent mark, with an average increase of 1 to 2 cent. However, actual sales merchants were unmoved and instead sold off, so the upward trend was not strong. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, due to the weather conditions, people's enthusiasm had waned. In addition, the wheat market had plummeted, and the bulls were also shaken. The selling pressure for all months was at its peak for a time. However, the price increases in recent days had been so rapid that the subsequent decline felt insignificant. As a result, this month was unchanged, June and July decreased slightly by 5 li, August decreased slightly by 2.5 li, September was unchanged, and October decreased slightly by 5 li, it is said.

Silk and Tea – High-Quality Early Cocoons in Chang'an Surge

Poor Cocoon Quality in Da Dian, Premium Cocoons Open at 50 Yuan

In the towns and villages near Chang'an, the early silkworm crops have all failed this year. The late crops have also been severely damaged by the cold and rainy weather during the peak leaf-eating period. The overall harvest of new cocoons is only 20% of a normal year, and the quality is inferior. Very few high-quality cocoons have arrived on the market. Only seven or eight cocoon shops have opened, with limited purchasing capacity. Each shop is competing to offer high prices for premium cocoons. Yesterday, improved-breed cocoons opened at 50.25 yuan, it is said.

Shanghai Factory Raw Silk Prices Struggle to Rise

Yesterday, the foreign firm silk market in Shanghai remained sluggish. Despite the frequent declines in the exchange rate, and the slightly higher prices telegraphed by overseas factories, the combined exchange rate made it difficult for prices to rise. Factories were less willing to sell. Yesterday, Mitsui purchased 10 bales of Shanghai white factory raw silk, Gan Li purchased 20 bales of Sichuan yellow factory raw silk, and Gao Pei purchased 8 bales of yellow coarse silk. Prices remained low, it is said.

New Tea Opening Prices in Wunan Await

New tea from Wuyi's southern villages is always picked and processed earlier than elsewhere. Since most mountain households are engaged in farming, they are busy planting rice at this time. They will harvest tea before the Start of Summer. Last year, due to the high prices in the northern mountain areas, tea merchants abandoned the nearby southern areas and headed north to purchase tea. Therefore, new tea from various villages in the southern area was quickly sold out last year, and prices were high. This year, although mountain households have already finished picking and are waiting to sell, tea merchants believe that the quality of tea in the southern route is inferior, and that the price of tea in the northern villages will not be as high as last year. They do not want to rush into buying and intend to wait and see how the new tea from the northern villages opens before setting prices, it is said.

Red and Green Tea Trend Downward Together

Yesterday in the foreign firms tea market, British firms showed strong interest in red teas from Qimen and Fuliang, and a total of 2,125 boxes were traded throughout the city. Trade was not lonely, but the prices offered by experts for medium and low-grade red teas were harsh, and the market fell by 30 to 40 taels. Local merchants of Zhenmei green tea, seeing that tea from other routes would soon arrive in Shanghai, feared that the market would be difficult to hold, and were willing to sell at lower prices. There was a downward trend of 10 to 20 taels, and the overall situation was not good, it is said.

New Tea Has Already Opened in Shangyu

Each mountain household in Yushan and Shangrao in the Gan region has already finished picking the early tea and closing the gardens. The production of the first tea is still good. Because banditry in the Changyu area has gradually subsided, farmers can pick tea with peace of mind. The harvest of the first tea in the two counties has increased compared to last year. Tea dealers from the local area and other ports have already begun buying and selling. A small number of tea shops in Hekou, Shangrao, Yucheng, Tongcun Street, and foreign firms are also active. Recently, the opening price of Yushan tea has been from 30 to 24 or 25 yuan per dan, but the quality is low. Other tea shops are not interested due to the sluggish sales of low-grade goods in the Shanghai market. The future of the tea market does not seem to be progressing, and mountain prices will be difficult to raise, it is said.
