Artistic Circles

Recent Canadian Literary Scene

— Man

Canada's national colors in literature are becoming increasingly strong, especially recently. This phenomenon can be said to be half due to the stimulation of Professor V.B. Rhodenizer. Rhodenizer's new "A Handbook on Canadian Literature" is the first comprehensive, fluent, concise, and fair treatise in this regard. He courageously pays special attention to modern works, believing that the superior position in novels should belong to the melancholy but not silent Swede, Frederick Philip Grove. As for the famous female writer Mazo de la Roche, he quite despises her, because she is superficial and lacks "realism." On the whole, this is indeed a valuable work. Only his view of valuing the genius of tragedy and despising the genius of comedy is the only shortcoming of the book.

Ms. Mazo de la Roche's new work "The Portrait of a Dog" is a moving biography depicting her beloved dog. This is a very beautifully written book that everyone who has read it likes, but some also feel it is a pity, thinking that she should continue to write her "Jalna" series, without having to change to write other works midway. This series of novels has now been written in its third volume, and can be published this fall. The whole book will be about four volumes. After completion, it will of course become a literary masterpiece of modern Canada.

Frederick Philip Grove's new work "The Yoke of Life" is the opposite of Mazo de la Roche. It is his most important and most superior work. In other words, it is his masterpiece. This is a very powerful novel, far superior in structure to his autobiographical "A Search for America," and exceeding his "Settlers of the Marsh" in breadth, depth, refinement, and diction. Because the themes are the same, if we want to compare this novel with other works, then only Hardy's "Jude the Obscure" can be used. However, Grove's novel is not an imitation of Hardy's, because he had not read a single line of Hardy's work when he wrote this novel.

In the modern Canadian literary scene, there is a strange figure who has reached the center of the Canadian literary scene from a side road. He is a French immigrant to Canada, but is now also recognized as a new figure in the French literary scene. This person is Maurice Constantin Weyer, who won the French Prix Goncourt two years ago. Weyer worked as a farmer in Manitoba, Canada for twelve years. In 1914, he abandoned everything and returned to his homeland to join the army. After the war, he returned to Canada again, but his own farm had become barren and dilapidated and could not be repaired. So he quickly ran to Paris and became a writer. Since his maiden work "A Man Scans his Past" won the Prix Goncourt, his literary career began. This novel is a work in the tradition of Goncourt. Except for a simple plot and a rigid background, there is nothing else. The background is Canada, but this Canada is only what the French see in their eyes, and the whole article is full of the abstract enthusiasm that the French like.

This amazing writer has written a completely different work this year, "A Martyr's Folly," which is purely local, just as his maiden work was purely foreign. This book is a biography in the form of a novel, written about the story of Louis Riel. Louis Riel was the leader of the rebels in the Northwest Rebellion of Canada in 1877 and 1885. The author used this person's frankness to depict how this enthusiastic and capable but chaotic young man became the leader of the struggling masses because of the mediocrity and incompetence of his kinsmen. The cause of the struggle was that the Hudson's Bay Company sold the land that is now western Canada to the colonial government, but did not take into account the rights of the local residents. Therefore, these residents resisted, and Louis Riel became their leader. He was not a capable person, but he finally won some preferential treatment for his people and full rights for their Roman Church. However, the British Protestants who suffered in the rebellion demanded that the murderers be arrested and severely punished. At this time, Riel's friends abandoned Riel and followed him to be arrested and hanged. His crime was "political, legal, religious assassination conspiracy."

War novels are still very popular in the modern Canadian literary scene. Among several first-class war novels, George A. Drew's "Canada's Fighting Airmen" is the most magnificent, but it is inevitably too much praise for the natives. This book contains ten stories, written about the achievements of Canada's top ten airmen in the European War. In August 1914, when the European War broke out, the British had less than one hundred combat aircraft. But by the time of the armistice, the number of aircraft used was more than 22,000, and the number of personnel used was 30,000, of which one-third were Canadians. According to official statistics, Canadian Bishop and Cole Shaw both had higher scores than any British air officer in destroying enemy aircraft. These two, along with Barker and McLaren, are four Canadians among the world's top ten airmen.

Contemporary issues have recently attracted the attention of Canadian writers, especially the issue of foreign trade. The famous

Canadian Satirist

Stephen Leacock has always been famous for his unique humorous and satirical articles, but unexpectedly, he is a professor of economics at a university. Recently, he published "Economic Prosperity in the British Empire," advocating that for the sake of British manufacturers, autonomous Canada should still be changed to a colony, directly under the jurisdiction of London, and should absorb 2 million British immigrants every year in order to solve the difficulty of the British population surplus. This is a truly appalling method, but it is said that Leacock is a comedian, so his economic monograph can only be regarded as a comedy novel. Although this painting has great value in enjoying British medals,

Thoughts After Seeing the 5th Morning Light Art Exhibition

— Guo Li

Before I express my thoughts, I want to state that I am an amateur when it comes to painting, so if there are any inappropriate words, please, fellow painters, do not laugh at me.

This day was May Day, so I was very happy to have the opportunity to see everyone's great works. When I arrived at the Morning Light Exhibition and went upstairs, the first thing I saw was Mr. Bao Yi's "Charcoal Sketch." Walking further ahead, I was startled. It turned out to be Mr. Hua Fu's "Red Terror" and Mr. Ying Peng's "Shooting" and "Hou Yi Shooting the Sun," as well as "Impression of Changsha." These works all stirred my soul, and I admired the greatness of the authors, who used their pens to depict a scene of life and vividly present it before our eyes. The authors used the crystallization of their passionate experiences, making us feel it in both body and soul. Indeed, only when painting reaches this level can it fully express the author's great personality. Furthermore, at this moment, I also remembered a saying from my friend Yuan Qing: "A successful work is truly the crystallization of the author's fresh blood." So many successful works, all made of fresh blood, are especially admirable given the difficulties faced by the comrades of the Morning Light Society.

As for the many works among them, they are all very good. Mr. Bao Yi's works, as expected of a veteran, show Mr. Chen's strength in composition, color, and brushstrokes. Especially that "Facial Sketch" truly has a special style, and the colors are even more extraordinary. Also, in my ignorant opinion, Mr. Ying Peng's "Shooting" has a style rarely seen in China. The colors are strong, giving a very stimulating feeling, and I also feel that it is somewhat similar to the style in the works of Franz Yon Stuck. That horse shooting is such an expression of beauty and strength. Not only that, but it also produces what the Japanese Takama calls intellectual art. Perhaps even these are not enough to describe it.

In addition, works such as "Trembling of the Night," "Wild Rose," "Crowd," "Flower Seller," "Victims," as well as "Peach Blossoms," "Jiangwan Road," "Fallen Leaves," "Continuation of the Sea Port," and "West Lake" all clearly show the various techniques, color schemes, compositions, and brushstrokes, revealing different unique styles. In short, this exhibition has at least given me very good knowledge, thoughts, and impressions. However, I also hope to see some works on patterns in the 6th exhibition. Perhaps this time it was inconvenient or for other reasons that they were not exhibited. I subjectively desire this at least, and also hope that all gentlemen will break the dullness of the current Chinese art world.

In short, there are other good works that are too numerous to mention. At the same time, I feel that my nonsense should also come to an end, otherwise, the more I talk, the more it will become a joke.

Art World Guidelines

(1) Articles are limited to news, reviews, and introductions of recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature at home and abroad.

(2) Photos are limited to recent portraits and works of domestic and foreign writers, and various photography related to (3)

(3) The number of words per article should not exceed 2,000.

Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

Youth Zone

Northern Journey Jottings

— An Nian

14. Fragments of Yanjing (Part 2)

The female dormitory is built entirely facing south. You can naturally imagine how bright and warm the house is when the sun shines through the windows. Males are not allowed to enter the female dormitory. The place for men and women to talk is Sister Hall. There are two Sister Halls in total, because the appearance and interior layout are the same, hence the name "Sister." The interior of Sister Hall is very exquisite. The gilded ceiling is like the houses in the imperial palace, except that the interior is a spacious room, not a box-like arrangement. This is indeed not a very intimate place for "romantic" aspirations. I heard that the Yanjing Weekly also discussed this matter for a period of time. People are naturally jealous, and those without a pair are in the majority, so the suggestion to divide Sister Hall into several boxes was finally rejected.

The women's gymnasium is very large. The men's gymnasium at Yanjing has not yet been fully completed. The men's gymnasium is built in the same style as the women's gymnasium. When I went to visit, the female instructor inside came out to greet me and was very polite.

The men's dormitory is generally facing west and east. In the middle is a lane with rooms on both sides. Only the sixth dormitory is like the female dormitory, with a single row of rooms facing south. In front of the sixth dormitory, there is a lake. This lake has become a very good scenic view for Yanjing University. In winter, the lake freezes and becomes a skating rink. In summer, willows hang around, and many small boats ripple on the water. Yanjing also has a water tower that is also very beautiful. It was originally a monotonous water tower, but because they wanted to decorate it to make it look better, they spent money and rebuilt it. The shadow of the tower reflected in the lake is very beautiful and moving.

The hospital in Yanjing is also very comfortable. Many people often pretend to be sick because they want to enjoy a few days of bliss in the hospital. Of course, those who pretend to be sick are not necessarily allowed to move into the hospital, but the comfort of the hospital can be imagined from this. The hospital is built behind a small hill and also has a sunbathing platform.

Every building in Yanjing has a telephone room. Many professors' houses are equipped with telephones. These telephones naturally refer to internal extensions. For example, if you want to visit a professor, you can call ahead to notify them, or if you want to call a classmate to chat, you can also call them. In addition, Yanjing also has internal mailboxes and another type of internal postage stamp, so transportation is also very convenient.

The professors at Yanjing probably each have a house. Besides Yanjing itself, the nearby areas are mostly residential areas for faculty, with so-called Yandong Garden, Yannan Garden, Tongfu, etc. There are also many large gardens, such as Dayuan, etc., which are inhabited by Yanjing faculty and staff. There are more than 280 faculty and staff at Yanjing. The residences of the professors alone number more than 100. These houses are all provided by the school.

Yanjing's library is naturally not as good as Tsinghua, and there are not as many books as in Tsinghua, but in terms of Chinese books, it is the best in the country, because the Columbia University and Harvard University in the United States have a Chinese Culture Research Association's book department, which is attached to Yanjing's library. They have plenty of money to buy those precious books.

If you haven't been to Yanjing, you must think that studying at Yanjing and buying books would be more expensive than at ordinary schools (because many of their books are original), but in fact, it is the opposite. It is common to not buy ten books in four years of study at Yanjing. In the first and second years, there may be a few basic books to buy, but in the third and fourth years, there is simply no need to buy a book. The reason is not that all courses require taking notes. To put it bluntly, all textbooks are provided by the school. Yanjing offers a very large number of courses each term. Because there are many courses offered, students are divided, and the number of students who select each course is reduced, so generally only about ten people attend each course, and the library has all the books used for each course. The library always has seven or eight copies of the same textbook. If only about ten people choose this course, then isn't it enough to have seven or eight copies of this book in the library?

These books cannot be borrowed, so if you want to prepare for class, you must go to the library.

Page 23

Youth Zone

Jiaotong University Female Students Establish Track and Field Team

— Quan

Since Ms. Sun Guiyun showed her talent at the National Games last year, all female students in the country know the importance of sports, and are unwilling to lag behind, actively rising up to engage in sports. Jiaotong University female students recently have a slogan, saying "Sun Guiyun is also a person, I am also a person. Guiyun can break the 100-meter record, can't I? There is Guiyun Bridge in Hangzhou, who knows if after this year's National Games in Nanjing, I can't have my name named on a Nanjing bridge? It is up to the person to do it."

Since the Jiaotong University female students have this grand ambition, they are particularly diligent in field events. There is a garden in front of the female dormitory, with a track around it. It was not very straight, but now, at the request of the female students, the sports authorities have instructed the engineering department to straighten it immediately, marking out the 100-meter line, 200-meter line, and 400-meter line.

Every morning, three ladies are constantly seen running in the garden. One is Ms. Li Xuan, who is petite but has a large stride. Unfortunately, she cannot last long. She is naturally adept at 50 meters and 100 meters. The second is Ms. Wu Shiying, who is from Guangdong. She previously studied at the First Girls' Middle School in Guangdong. At that time, her 100-meter time was 15 seconds, winning first place. Now, because she has not trained for a long time, her performance has declined when she first tried. The third is Ms. Hou Yufen. Ms. Hou is very good at sprinting, with a graceful starting posture. Her 100-meter time is about 14 seconds. The three ladies have now invited Mr. Chen Yutian, a graduate of the school, a famous football player and sprinter in Shanghai, to coach them. Mr. Chen comes to the school three times a week, teaching them everything about starting methods, stride length, and all postures, and has also ordered a textbook for textual teaching.

In terms of track events, in addition to sprinting, there is also the low hurdles event, which is also being prepared for training and joining. The trainees are Ms. Tao Chun and Ms. Wu Shu, but they have not officially started yet.

In terms of field events, there are three events: shot put, long jump, and high jump. Shot put is the forte of Ms. Wu Shiying and Ms. Hou Yufen. They can throw casually and achieve results of 8 or 9 meters. The instructor for the long jump event is still Mr. Chen Yutian. Those who have joined the training are Ms. Li Xuan, Ms. Zhu Yaozhen, and Ms. Wen Jie. Although the results in the high jump event are not high, there are many trainees, including Wang Hengling, Zhu Yaozhen, Wen Jie, Wu Shu, Tao Chun, etc., seven or eight people.

In total, there are twelve members of the track and field team. It has now been organized, and Ms. Hou Minfen has been elected as the captain, Ms. Wu Shiying as the manager, and Mr. Wang, a male student, as the secretary. At this year's Jiangda Games, because the school's female students are just starting out, except for Ms. Hou's and Ms. Wu's sprinting and Ms. Hou's shot put, they are not very confident in the rest, so only Ms. Hou and Ms. Wu were sent as representatives. In the preliminary round on the first day, both were selected. Although they only scored one point in the finals, it seemed even more glorious compared to the blank scores of Guanghua and other schools. It is heard that the team secretary said that the team captain recently issued three rules: (1) No absence from training without reason. (2) No joking or playing during training. (3) No disobedience to the instructor's guidance. Violations will result in a warning for the first offense, a serious warning for the second offense, a warning from the sports authorities for the third offense, and a deduction of one sports credit from the sports authorities for the fourth offense to show punishment, it is said.

A Disturbing Lesson

— Cheng

"Di, what is this class?" Wei said urgently, looking at the letter she had just received.

"Oh, how come you don't know? This class is what you call the 'optional class.' Now, are you going to write love letters again?" Di, with an envious and mocking face, smiled at Wei.

"Yes, I'm naturally writing love letters. Why don't you take some time to write to your lover, Ruo? You know, he's longing for you," Wei said triumphantly, taking out blue ink, a pen, and stationery from the desk.

"What's there to long for or not? I never want to do what you do, putting aside books and focusing all my attention on writing love letters. I honestly tell you, although I also like to be in love and have a lover, I definitely don't want to put aside any subject. I believe that since we are students now, we should put the idea of studying above everything else..."

"Okay, okay, Ms. Di, please stop! I already understand your 'doctrine.' I remember you've preached it several times," Wei said, looking at her solemn back.

"Don't make any noise. If the old man comes in to teach and hears you, wouldn't it be embarrassing?" This was the accent of Ms. Hong from Beiping. She was very focused on reading a copy of "The Vanguard Monthly." Probably, she was confused by their noises, so she suddenly came out to stop them.

"What's embarrassing? Look at him himself..." Wei was about to get excited and continue speaking, but Mr. Ke's head had already stretched into the classroom door. She saw him, shrank her head, shrugged her shoulders, and quickly lowered her head, pretending that she was originally writing a letter.

"Ge..." Mr. Ke tapped his leather shoe heel loudly on the podium, called the roll, and opened the book to start the class. He first drew several connected triangles on the blackboard, and then slowly taught us in English, "Because this angle is a right angle, so that angle is like this, and that angle is like that..." Several good students who scored a hundred and ninety in geometry also happily agreed with him. Several students who did not score as well as them coldly shouted, "I don't understand, I don't understand. Please explain it again, explain it more clearly." So Mr. Ke stared incredulously at the students who shouted and repeated the teaching of this angle and that angle.

Suddenly, Ms. Qin, with a drawn-out throat, said in a melodious voice, "This kind of geometry is really confusing. It's hard enough to understand it, but after a few days, I'll return it all to you. What's the use of us reading it? Moreover, studying this kind of geometry is the most boring thing." She usually listened to Mr. Ke's lecture haphazardly in geometry class, if she had already finished writing a reply to her lover. Otherwise, she was just like Wei, willing to sacrifice her homework and wholeheartedly write love letters.

"Qin, you're wrong. Studying geometry is really interesting. If you find it boring, you should blame yourself for not... Usually in this class, you don't often write... Don't you think it's useless and unworthy of studying?" Ying felt that saying the word love letter was very embarrassing, so she quickly changed the meaning. She was one of Mr. Ke's favorites, always handing in her paper first for every exam, and her grades were the best.

"You've given your heart to your lover, so naturally you'll find geometry tasteless." This was the instruction of another geometry king. She spoke the word lover in a particularly low voice and glanced at Mr. Ke.

"Don't be hypocritical. Mr. Ke, you see many students writing love letters, but you don't care at all," Di told the teacher unfairly, after she finished copying the geometry proof on the blackboard and heard them arguing too noisily. She might have been thinking, "Several sloppy students are happily and sweetly writing love letters. I'll write too, but I don't want to put it down. If I listen to the teacher, I won't be able to concentrate because of their noise."

"Okay, everyone be quiet and listen to me. I know some of you are writing letters. I don't forbid them. First, I originally hoped that they would realize it themselves. Second, the 'love' of young people is the easiest to be moved, the richest, and the most passionate. If I ignorantly forbid them, they would have to stop writing. But if their hearts still don't stop, or even burn more passionately, what I teach won't enter their ears. Then, why should I force them to sit there for an hour? So, my idea is only to let it be natural. Listen to me if you want to listen, don't listen if you don't want to listen. Everything is up to you. Anyway, people who are not interested will never learn well in their lifetime."

"But, that's not right, Mr. Ke. How do you know if a person is interested or not?" Ms. Hong from Beiping asked, seemingly refuting and doubting.

"That's very simple. Those who are interested will put everything aside and listen to me," he said, wiping the words off the blackboard, intending to teach the next section.

Wei suddenly thought of something and said urgently, "Mr. Ke, you say that the 'love' of young people is the easiest to be moved and the most passionate, then I ask you, how is your 'love'?" Wei smiled cheekily at Mr. Ke's glowing face.

"Don't make noise. I'm going to teach the next section. It will be tested. It's very important," Mr. Ke quickly said several "important" words in a row. As for Wei's question, it could be considered an answer.

"Leave it for next time. The section you taught today is enough to make our brains confused."

"Mr. Ke, there are only ten minutes left. Give us a break."

"Teaching too much is like eating too much food, it can't be digested."

"………………………………"

It was noisy and disturbing, like what the teacher said, we were like a "teahouse."

"Then, if you don't want to teach, then don't teach. Anyway, the teacher is a servant of the students, and everything is up to you."

"Oh, no, we're afraid that teaching too much will only make what we already understand confusing," Hong and many classmates said.

"In short, you never tire of reading and writing love letters. You are willing to use 'love' to bewitch yourself and bind yourself. As for geometry or other subjects, you are not willing to do it as dedicatedly as you do with love letters."

"Mr. Ke, it seems that you are also bewitched by 'love.' In your book clip, there is a very beautiful……………… photo," Wei said with a smile, as if unable to bear it.

"Who said it's a lover? No, no. Don't talk nonsense. Since we're not going to continue teaching, let's dismiss class," Mr. Ke's face gradually flushed. He quickly left the classroom. At that time, the dismissal bell had not yet rung, but a burst of enthusiastic cheers replaced it.

A Sound of "Hang Yu"... and Others

— Yi

Datong University has always held the purpose of "saving the country through reading" and has very few opportunities to contact the outside world, so Datong in the West Gate school district, the general public does not pay much attention to the existence of this institution of higher learning. Therefore, news about Datong is not easily heard.

But now it is different. On the one hand, they are still working hard on scholarship, and at the same time, they have a tendency to be active with the outside world, full of vitality, especially in the effort of material construction. Last semester, a sound of "Hang Yu" broke the silence in the air. Listening to lectures in the classroom, one could still faintly hear the lingering sound of them—coolies. Students hoped for the end of the "Hang Yu" sound every day, yearning for a magnificent gymnasium, which was completed in February this year for the 20th anniversary. The area is wide.
